                                PUBLIC PARTICIPATION GUIDELINES
Board of Education meetings are held in person in the board room located at 3738 Walnut Avenue, Carmichael,
California. Alternatively, you can view the board meeting virtually via livestream from a computer, mobile device
or tablet at https://www.sanjuan.edu/boardmeeting. The district has taken the following steps to assist the public in
offering public comment:

     1. In Person Public Comment. Public comment may be offered in person during the board meeting at the
        district office located at 3738 Walnut Avenue, Carmichael, California. Board Bylaw 9323 limits visitor
        comments to two (2) minutes per speaker, with no more than 30 minutes per single topic. Time will be
        extended for any speaker who uses an interpreter. Please be aware that public comments, including your
        name, become part of the public record.
     2. Online Submission of Public Comment. Members of the public may submit written comments by using the
        comment form located on the district website at http://www.sanjuan.edu/boardmeeting. If you wish to
        submit a written comment on more than one agenda item, please submit a separate form for each item on
        which you are commenting. Written comments are limited to 1,500 characters. Comments will be provided
        to the members of the board.

                                  NOTE: The times indicated are approximate.
The Board of Education welcomes and encourages the public’s participation at the board meetings and has devoted
time throughout the meeting for that purpose. You may comment on items included on this agenda; however, we
ask that you limit your comments to two (2) minutes, so that as many people as possible may be heard (Education
Code section 35145.5, Government Code section 54954.3).

A person with a disability may contact the Board of Education office at (916) 971-7111, or email
stephanie.cunningham@sanjuan.edu at least 48 hours before the scheduled board meeting to request receipt of an
agenda and other distributed writings in an appropriate alternative format, or to request disability-related
modifications or accommodations, including auxiliary aids or services, in order to participate in the public board
meeting.

Translation and interpretation services will be made available upon request with advance notice. If you wish to
utilize these services, please notify the Board of Education office at (916) 971-7111, or email
stephanie.cunningham@sanjuan.edu at least 24 hours before the scheduled board meeting to allow for the
scheduling of appropriate translation staff and other resources.

                                                Mission Statement
We partner with our San Juan Unified community in setting high expectations for academic achievement rooted in
equity and unity to create supportive learning experiences in which all students, families and staff can excel and
thrive.

                                   San Juan Unified Land Acknowledgement


                                                                                                                     4
The San Juan Unified School District acknowledges that our schools are located on the ancestral lands of the
Nisenan and Miwok peoples, who continue to care for this land as they have since time immemorial. We deeply
respect their ongoing connection to this land and recognize their resilience in preserving and revitalizing their
cultures and traditions despite historical and ongoing challenges.

We recognize the profound injustices endured by their ancestors, including genocide, forced assimilation, and
displacement, and we remain aware of the ongoing challenges and injustices they face today. As we advance in our
commitment to equity and inclusion, we pledge to strengthen our connections by fostering a culture of
understanding, respect, and active collaboration with their communities.

                                            Board of Education Minutes
                                                 March 25, 2025

Regular Meeting
Board of Education
5:15 p.m.

Open Session/Call to Order (A)
The March 25 regular meeting was called to order by the president, Ben Avey. The board meeting was held in person and
was also livestreamed on the district website.

Roll Call
Present:
Ben Avey, president
Tanya Kravchuk, vice president
Manuel Perez, clerk
Zima Creason, member
Nick Bloise, member
Abid Stanekzai, member
Absent:
Pam Costa, member

Announcement of Closed Session Topics/Closed Session Visitor Comments (A-1)
There were no closed session visitor comments.

Closed Session (B)
The meeting was then recessed with the board convening in closed session to consider a student expulsion in one case
(Education Code section 48918[f]); to discuss with negotiator Daniel Thigpen, Executive Director, Labor Relations and
Government Affairs, regarding CSEA Chapter 127 General/Operations support, Chauffeurs/Teamsters Local No. 150
Transportation, Supervisors, Teachers and Certificated Supervisory units, and regarding non-represented groups:
management and confidential units (Government Code section 54957.6); and to conference with legal counsel – anticipated
litigation: significant exposure to litigation (Government Code section 54956.9(d)(2) and (4)).

Reconvene Open Session/Pledge of Allegiance (C)
At 6:30 p.m., the March 25 regular meeting was called back to order by the president, Ben Avey. Two members of the Del
Campo High School Jr. ROTC led the group in the Pledge of Allegiance.

Minutes Approved (D)
It was moved by Mr. Perez, seconded by Mr. Bloise, that the minutes of the March 11 regular meeting be approved.
MOTION CARRIED 6-0-1 [AYES: Avey, Kravchuk, Perez, Creason, Bloise, Stanekzai; NOES: None: ABSENT: Costa].

Recognition: Week of the Young Child (E-1)
It was moved by Mr. Stanekzai, seconded by Ms. Creason, to adopt Resolution No. A-449, proclaiming the week of April
5-11, 2025, as the Week of the Young Child. MOTION CARRIED 6-0-1 [AYES: Avey, Kravchuk, Perez, Creason, Bloise,
Stanekzai; NOES: None: ABSENT: Costa].



                                                                                                                 2667
                                                                                                                          6
Recognition: School Library Month (E-2)
It was moved by Ms. Kravchuk, seconded by Mr. Perez, to adopt Resolution No. A-450, recognizing the month of April as
School Library Month. MOTION CARRIED 6-0-1 [AYES: Avey, Kravchuk, Perez, Creason, Bloise, Stanekzai; NOES:
None: ABSENT: Costa].

Recognition: Adult Education Week (E-3)
It was moved by Ms. Creason, seconded by Mr. Stanekzai, to adopt Resolution No. A-451, recognizing the week of April
6-12, 2025, as Adult Education Week. MOTION CARRIED 6-0-1 [AYES: Avey, Kravchuk, Perez, Creason, Bloise,
Stanekzai; NOES: None: ABSENT: Costa].

High School Student Council Reports (F-1)
High School Student Council representatives Madison Stewart and Ella Gustafson from Casa Roble Fundamental High
School and Morgan Reed and Maddie Hollander from Rio Americano High School updated the board on the goals, activities
and achievements at their respective schools.

Closed Session/Expulsion Actions (F-6)
Mr. Perez reported that the board voted unanimously to accept a hearing panel’s recommendation of one stipulated
expulsion in case number M-19.

Visitor Comments (G)
Christine McCann-Kenney expressed concerns about the reduction in hours for instructional assistants.

Rebecca Duditch expressed support for the work of instructional assistants.

Sherry Skelly Griffith shared information about the San Juan Education Foundation’s scholarship program.

Tim Thayer spoke about English learners who lack preparation in mathematics.

Fay Grundel spoke about school librarians and school libraries.

Derek Newell provided an update on Options for Youth Charter School.

Consent Calendar Approved (H-1/H-6)
It was moved by Mr. Stanekzai, seconded by Ms. Kravchuk, that the consent calendar items H-1 through H-6 be approved.
MOTION CARRIED 6-0-1 [AYES: Avey, Kravchuk, Perez, Creason, Bloise, Stanekzai; NOES: None: ABSENT: Costa].

Personnel (H-1)
Appointments, leaves of absence and separations – approved as submitted.

Purchasing Report (H-2)
Purchase orders, service agreements and contracts; change orders/amendments; construction and public works bids and
contracts; and piggyback contracts – approved as submitted.

Business/Financial Report (H-3)
Warrants and payroll and notices of completion – approved as submitted.

Gifts (H-4)
Acceptance of gifts to Bella Vista High School and Encina High School.

Surplus Property (H-5)
Approval to dispose of surplus property pursuant to Board Policy 3270 and Education Code sections 17545 and 17546.

Head Start and Early Head Start Grant Application 2025-2026 (H-6)
Approval of the submission and implementation of, if funded, the Head Start and Early Head Start Grant 2025-2026.

New High School Courses for 2025-2026 (J-1)
Interim Deputy Superintendent of Schools and Student Support Amy Slavensky, Ph.D., presented the topic and then
introduced Director of Professional Learning and Curriculum Innovation Nicole Kukral. Ms. Kukral explained the new
course request process, the goals for new courses and reviewed the list of new proposed high school courses for 2025-2026
which includes: Science: The Science of Food; Mathematics: Financial Math, Math Modeling, Traffic Analysis and

                                                                                                                    2668
                                                                                                                            7
Engineering; English: Middle Years Programme (MYP) 4 Language and Literature: Ethnic Studies, English 9: Ethnic
Studies; Social Studies: Chicano Studies, Middle Years Programme (MYP) 5 United States History and Ethnic Studies;
Art: Music and Ethnic Studies; Career Technical Education: Animation I: Introduction to Animation; Animation II:
Intermediate; Animation III: Advanced; College Preparatory Electives: Advanced Placement (AP) African American
Studies; Podcasting and Storytelling; Science Olympiad; Principles of Athletic Performance; English Language
Development (ELD) IV; International Baccalaureate Career-related Programme (IBCP) 2 Personal and Professional Skills;
and Adult Education: Job Readiness. Board members made comments and posed questions, which Ms. Kukral addressed.
Ms. Creason inquired about the animation series and the adult education job readiness course. Ms. Kravchuk spoke about
community feedback, the ethnic studies mandate, resources for technology courses and the new course request process. Mr.
Avey commented on course options for block versus traditional high schools. Action was scheduled for April 8.

Bond Project Update (J-2)
Chief Operations Officer Frank Camarda presented the topic and introduced Director of Facilities, Construction &
Modernization Nicholas Arps who provided an update about the district’s past, present and future construction projects
funded by the 2016 Measure P Bond. Mr. Arps also discussed smaller-scale projects, including classroom furniture
replacement and maintenance and operations light modifications. Board members made comments and posed questions,
which staff addressed. Mr. Perez expressed appreciation for the projects at Mesa Verde High School, Sylvan Middle School,
San Juan High School and Encina High School. Ms. Creason thanked the team for its efforts. Ms. Kravchuk inquired
whether shade structures are an option at stadiums. Mr. Bloise expressed support for the use of the bond dollars. Mr. Avey
spoke about swimming pools on all high school campuses.

Technology Update (J-3)
Senior Director of Technology Peter Skibitzki provided an overview of the various functions and projects of the Technology
Services Department. Mr. Skibitzki explained the department’s customer service philosophy and discussed the work of the
five teams within Technology Services. Mr. Skibitzki also shared information regarding the E-Rate program, cybersecurity
threats and protection, and artificial intelligence. Mr. Skibitzki also outlined the end-of-year planning. Board members
commended staff on the department’s work, offering comments and posed questions, which Mr. Skibitzki addressed.

Public Hearing: Resolution No. 4197 Bella Vista High School Student Safety Project (J-4)
Chief Operations Officer Frank Camarda presented the item. Mr. Avey declared the topic of the Bella Vista High School
student safety project #206-9716-P1 being proposed for submission for funding, as per Education Code section 101460(b),
a public hearing and invited the public to speak. There being no questions or comments from the public, Mr. Avey declared
the public hearing closed. It was moved by Mr. Stanekzai, seconded by Mr. Bloise, to adopt Resolution No. 4197,
authorizing and approving project #206-9716-P1. MOTION CARRIED 6-0-1 [AYES: Avey, Kravchuk, Perez, Creason,
Bloise, Stanekzai; NOES: None: ABSENT: Costa].

Public Hearing: Resolution No. 4198 Andrew Carnegie Middle School Student Safety Project (J-5)
Mr. Camarda presented the item. Mr. Avey declared the topic of the Andrew Carnegie Middle School student safety project
#061-9716-P1 being proposed for submission for funding, as per Education Code section 101460(b), a public hearing and
invited the public to speak. There being no questions or comments from the public, Mr. Avey declared the public hearing
closed. It was moved by Ms. Kravchuk, seconded by Mr. Bloise, to adopt Resolution No. 4198, authorizing and approving
project #061-9716-P1. MOTION CARRIED 6-0-1 [AYES: Avey, Kravchuk, Perez, Creason, Bloise, Stanekzai; NOES:
None: ABSENT: Costa].

Public Hearing: Resolution No. 4199 Mary Deterding Elementary School Student Safety Project (J-6)
Mr. Camarda presented the item. Mr. Avey declared the topic of the Mary Deterding Elementary School student safety
project #112-9716-P1 being proposed for submission for funding, as per Education Code section 101460(b), a public
hearing and invited the public to speak. There being no questions or comments from the public, Mr. Avey declared the
public hearing closed. It was moved by Ms. Creason, seconded by Mr. Perez, to adopt Resolution No. 4199, authorizing
and approving project #112-9716-P1. MOTION CARRIED 6-0-1 [AYES: Avey, Kravchuk, Perez, Creason, Bloise,
Stanekzai; NOES: None: ABSENT: Costa].

Public Hearing: Resolution No. 4200 Pasadena Avenue Elementary School Student Safety Project (J-7)
Mr. Camarda presented the item. Mr. Avey declared the topic of the Pasadena Avenue Elementary School student safety
project #141-9716-P1 being proposed for submission for funding, as per Education Code section 101460(b), a public
hearing and invited the public to speak. There being no questions or comments from the public, Mr. Avey declared the
public hearing closed. It was moved by Mr. Bloise, seconded by Mr. Perez, to adopt Resolution No. 4200, authorizing and
approving project #141-9716-P1. MOTION CARRIED 6-0-1 [AYES: Avey, Kravchuk, Perez, Creason, Bloise, Stanekzai;
NOES: None: ABSENT: Costa].


                                                                                                                    2669
                                                                                                                             8
Public Hearing: Resolution No. 4201 Pershing Elementary School Student Safety Project (J-8)
Mr. Camarda presented the item. Mr. Avey declared the topic of the Pershing Elementary School student safety project
#158-9716-P1 being proposed for submission for funding, as per Education Code section 101460(b), a public hearing and

None: ABSENT: Costa].

Revisions to Governance Handbook (J-9)
Chief of Staff Trent Allen presented the proposed revisions to the Governance Handbook. Board members engaged in a
discussion regarding the professional development language that was proposed at the February 25, 2025, board meeting,
specifically the expectation that board members complete the California School Boards Association (CSBA) Masters in
Governance (MIG) program in order to move into a leadership position on the board. Board members agreed to modify the
language to read: “Prior to serving in an officer role, a member is expected to be enrolled in, and actively working to
complete, CSBA’s Masters in Governance program.” Mr. Avey also inquired about the section of the handbook related to
assigning work to staff. Superintendent Bassanelli explained that board member information requests need to go through
her in order to ensure responsiveness and transparency. Ms. Creason noted that this process is a normal business protocol
and is not unique to the district. It was moved by Mr. Perez, seconded by Ms. Creason, to approve the proposed revisions
to the Governance Handbook as amended. MOTION CARRIED 6-0-1 [AYES: Avey, Kravchuk, Perez, Creason, Bloise,
Stanekzai; NOES: None: ABSENT: Costa].

Board Reports (K)
Mr. Bloise reported that he visited Del Campo High School, where he learned about their Career Technical Education
programs, and he thanked staff for fixing the sign at Del Campo.

Ms. Kravchuk shared that tomorrow she will take part in a regional CSBA delegate assembly phone call and asked if board
members had anything they would like her to uplift during the call.

Mr. Avey reported that he attended the CSBA president’s workshop, and then he invited Mr. Allen to share information
about the recent California School Public Relations Association (CalSPRA) awards that staff received.

Future Agenda (L)
There were no items added to the future agenda.

Adjournment (N)
At 8:40 p.m., there being no further business, the regular meeting was adjourned.

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                      AGENDA ITEM:                      E.1
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                      MEETING DATE:                  04/08/2025

SUBJECT: California School Bus Driver's Appreciation Day

DEPARTMENT: Human Resources

ACTION REQUESTED:
Action: The superintendent is recommending that the board adopt Resolution No. A-452 proclaiming April 22,
2025, as California School Bus Driver’s Appreciation Day.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
Annually, on the fourth Tuesday of April, the State of California officially recognizes all school bus drivers for
their continued and excellent services to the youth of the State. The district’s bus drivers are deserving of special
public recognition and the highest commendations; thus, the district also traditionally adopts a resolution
proclaiming the fourth Tuesday of April as School Bus Driver’s Appreciation Day.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. Resolution No. A-452

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A

PREVIOUS STAFF/BOARD ACTION:
Superintendent's Cabinet: 03/31/2025

FISCAL IMPACT:
N/A

PREPARED BY:                 Daniel Thigpen, Acting Chief of Human Resources

APPROVED BY:                 Melissa Bassanelli, Superintendent of Schools




                                                                                                                        10
                                         SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT

                                                     Resolution No. A-452

                            CALIFORNIA SCHOOL BUS DRIVER’S APPRECIATION DAY
                                              April 22, 2025

         WHEREAS, annually, on the fourth Tuesday of April, the people of California should officially recognize all school
bus drivers for their continued and excellent services to the youth of the State, and these drivers are deserving of special public
recognition and the highest commendations; and

        WHEREAS, the safety of our children rests in the hands of trained school bus drivers for up to two or three hours
each school day; and

         WHEREAS, personal time and energy are expended by school bus drivers in their initial training, maintaining a
current license, perfecting their driving skills, and accruing added knowledge of school bus laws through continuing education
classes; and

         WHEREAS, school bus drivers, through counseling and disciplinary techniques, are sometimes asked to assist the
students in appropriate interactive peer and adult behavior; and

        WHEREAS, school bus drivers often face natural and unexpected hazards in the performance of their duties; and

       WHEREAS, school bus drivers exhibit patience and kindness toward students, parents, and school staff in the
performance of their duties; and

       WHEREAS, school bus drivers consistently demonstrate an awareness of, and direct attention to, the mechanical
maintenance of the school bus and safety conditions of the school bus routes; and

         WHEREAS, many school bus drivers perform their services for thousands and thousands of accident- free miles, year
after year.

        NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the San Juan Unified School District Board of Education hereby
proudly proclaims April 22, 2025, as California’s School Bus Driver’s Appreciation Day to be celebrated by the district and
community.

Attested to this
8th Day of April, 2025
                                                                     Ben Avey, President

SUBJECT: Surplus Property

DEPARTMENT: Fiscal Services

ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board approve the disposal of surplus property pursuant to Board
Policy 3270.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The Governing Board recognizes that the district may own personal property, which is unusable, obsolete, or no
longer needed by the district. The superintendent or designee shall arrange for the sale or disposal of district
personal property in accordance with board policy and the requirements or state law.

The superintendent or designee shall identify to the board all items not needed by the district together with their
estimated value and a recommended disposition.

      RESOLUTION BEFORE THE SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT
    BOARD OF EDUCATION APPROVING LEASE AMENDMENT NO.2 FOR THE
         ENCINA HIGH SCHOOL FULL SITE RENOVATION PROJECT
                      SJUSD PROJECT #202-9332-Pl

                                   RESOLUTION NO. 4194


WHEREAS, sections 17406 of the Education Code authorize school districts, including the San
Juan Unified School District ("District"), to use the lease-leaseback procurement process; and

WHEREAS, the District Board of Education ("Board") previously approved the award of the
Site Lease and Facilities Lease to Core West, Inc. dba as Core Construction for this Project,
including preconstruction services in the amount of $95,000.00; and

WHEREAS, Phase #1 - Light Modernization of the project insurance policy is amended to a
Non-OCIP insurance coverage requirement.

NOW, THEREFORE, the San Juan Unified School District Board of Education does hereby
resolve as follows:

Section 1. The foregoing recitals are hereby adopted as true and correct.

Section 2. The Board approves the Total Base Rent in the amount of $3,174,292.00 as per
Amendment #2.

Original Facilities Lease Amount- Preconstruction Services                           $95,000.00
Net Change by Amendment #1                                                        $3,117,287.00
Net Changed by Amendment #2                                                 $57,005.00 $57,0005
Revised Total Base Rent                                                           $3,174,292.00
Revised Facilities Lease Amount                                                   $3,269,292.00


The foregoing findings and decision to award were made by the San Juan Unified School District
Board of Education at a meeting of the Board on February 25th, 2025, by the following vote:

      RESOLUTION BEFORE THE SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT
    BOARD OF EDUCATION APPROVING LEASE AMENDMENT NO.2 FOR THE
         ENCINA HIGH SCHOOL FULL SITE RENOVATION PROJECT
                      SJUSD PROJECT #202-9332-P1

                                   RESOLUTION NO. 4194


WHEREAS, sections 17406 of the Education Code authorize school districts, including the San
Juan Unified School District (“District”), to use the lease-leaseback procurement process; and

WHEREAS, the District Board of Education (“Board”) previously approved the award of the
Site Lease and Facilities Lease to Core West, Inc. dba as Core Construction for this Project,
including preconstruction services in the amount of $95,000.00; and

WHEREAS, Phase #1 – Light Modernization of the project insurance policy is amended to a
Non-OCIP insurance coverage requirement.

NOW, THEREFORE, the San Juan Unified School District Board of Education does hereby
resolve as follows:

Section 1. The foregoing recitals are hereby adopted as true and correct.

Section 2. The Board approves the Total Base Rent in the amount of $3,174,292.00 as per
Amendment #2.

Original Facilities Lease Amount– Preconstruction Services                         $95,000.00
Net Change by Amendment #1                                                      $3,117,287.00
Net Changed by Amendment #2                                                        $57,005.00
Revised Total Base Rent                                                         $3,174,292.00
Revised Facilities Lease Amount                                                 $3,269,292.00


The foregoing findings and decision to award were made by the San Juan Unified School District
Board of Education at a meeting of the Board on April 8th, 2025, by the following vote:

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                     AGENDA ITEM:                     H.7
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                     MEETING DATE:                04/08/2025

SUBJECT: Bella Vista High School Site Security Project CEQA Categorical Exemption

DEPARTMENT: Operations

ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board approve the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA)
Notice of Exemption for the Bella Vista High School Site Security Project.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The proposed project is located entirely within Bella Vista High School’s campus at 8301 Madison Avenue (APN:
249-0020-002-0000), in Fair Oaks, California. The project area spans approximately 5,653 square feet and 488 feet
of primarily landscaped and paved areas within the school’s boundaries. The project scope includes the installation
of new ornamental and chain link fencing and maintenance, pipe, and double gates throughout the school campus,
as well as the relocation of the existing bike enclosure.

As the actions associated with the proposed project are not expected to result in a significant environmental
impact, it is expected that this project is exempt under the Class XI Categorical Exemption (Accessory Structures)
and Class XIV Categorical Exemption (Minor Additions to Schools), as described in the California Code of
Regulations, Title 15, Section 15300 et seq.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. CEQA Categorical Exemption

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A
PREVIOUS STAFF/BOARD ACTION:
Superintendent's Cabinet: 03/31/2025

FISCAL IMPACT:
N/A

PREPARED BY:                Nicholas Arps, Director, Facilities, Construction and Modernization

APPROVED BY:                Frank Camarda, Chief Operations Officer
                            Melissa Bassanelli, Superintendent of Schools

RE:             Bella Vista High School Site Security Project
                CEQA Categorical Exemption
                Terracon Project No: NB257045



Project Information:
The proposed project is located entirely within Bella Vista High                 8301 Madison Avenue
(APN: 249-0020-002-0000), in Fair Oaks, California. The project area spans approximately 5,653 square
feet and 488 feet of primarily landscaped and paved areas within               boundaries (Exhibit 1).
The project scope includes the installation of new ornamental and chain link fencing and maintenance,
pipe, and double gates throughout the school campus, as well as the relocation of the existing bike
enclosure.

As the actions associated with the proposed project are not expected to result in a significant
environmental impact, it is expected that this project is exempt under the Class XI Categorical
Exemption (Accessory Structures) and Class XIV Categorical Exemption (Minor Additions to Schools),
as described in the California Code of Regulations, Title 15, Section 15300 et seq.


Legal Setting:
Categorical Exemptions (Cal. Code Regs. tit. 14 § 15300)
Projects that are not expected to result in a significant environmental impact may be Categorically
Exempt from the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) review. As described in Cal. Code Regs.
tit. 14 § 15300, Section 21084 of the Public Resources Code requires these guidelines to include a list
of classes of projects which have been determined not to have a significant effect on the environment
and which shall, therefore, be exempt from the provisions of CEQA. In response to that mandate, the
Secretary for Resources has found that the following classes of projects listed in this article do not have
a significant effect on the environment, and they are declared to be categorically exempt from the
requirement for the preparation of environmental documents.

Like many school-renovation projects (that do not involve additional classrooms or student capacity),
the proposed project is not expected to result in any significant environmental impacts under CEQA.
Table 1 provides an abbreviated CEQA checklist, explaining why the implementation of the proposed
project would not result in any significant environmental impacts.

 Impact Category       Description

                       The proposed project would not result in impacts related to scenic vistas, state-
                       listed scenic highways as the nearest scenic location is the California State Route
 Aesthetics            160, approximately 30 miles southeast of campus. Further, it would not require
                       the installation of equipment that would be inconsistent with previous
                       conditions; and would not result in an impact on Aesthetics.

 Agriculture and
                    The proposed project would not involve agricultural lands or Prime Farmland.
 Forestry Resources

                       The proposed project would not result in the exposure of pollutants or odors to
                       sensitive receptors. Although Sacramento County is in nonattainment status for
                       PM-2.5 (2006) and 8-Hour Ozone (2015) criteria pollutants, the proposed project
                       would not result in a significant net increase of such pollutants, nor would the
                       project conflict with the Sacramento Metropolitan Air Quality Management
 Air Quality

                       Plan (SIP) as the emissions would be associated with the limited use of
                       construction equipment. The equipment required to install new fencing and
                       gates and to relocate a bike enclosure utilize smaller engines and would be
                       operated as needed for a limited amount of time.

                       The project area is not expected to provide habitat for federally- or state-listed
 Biological            species, nor would it affect a Habitat Conservation Plan (HCP), Natural
 Resources             Community Conservation Planning (NCCP), or other sensitive biological
                       resources.

                       The project does not contain known historic properties and is not suspected to
                       contain archeological artifacts as the general area is previously developed. If
 Cultural Resources    archeological or cultural resources are discovered onsite, work would cease
                       immediately until consultation and approval to continue work was provided by a
                       qualified archaeologist.

                       The proposed project would not result in an impact related to the wasteful or
 Energy                inefficient use of energy since the project will not require the use of equipment
                       with high energy requirements during its operations.

                       The proposed project would not result in geological impacts. The project
 Geology and Soils     construction would take place on previously developed and disturbed land and
                       would not result in new construction in unsafe soils.

                       the proposed project would not have a significant effect on transportation since
 Transportation        construction will be small-scale and confined to the campus. Further,
                       construction will occur outside of the school year when student traffic patterns
                       would not be affected by the work.

Bella Vista High School Site Security | Fair Oaks, California

                        The proposed project would not have the capability to impact a listed or eligible
 Tribal Cultural        resource as there are no known relationships to the site; however, if resources

                        The proposed project does not involve Wildfire Hazards since the project will not

 Mandatory              The proposed project does not have the potential to substantially degrade or
 Findings of            reduce the habitat of a species or impact known resources. The project would
 Significance           not result in a cumulatively considerable contribution to a cumulative impact.


Exceptions (Cal. Code Regs. tit. 14 § 15300.2)
It should be noted that six (6) exceptions are described, which if applicable to a project, would disqualify
the project from the usage of a Categorical Exemption. These exceptions are:

(a) Location. Classes 3, 4, 5, 6, and 11 are qualified by consideration of where the project is to be
located a project that is ordinarily insignificant in its impact on the environment may in a particularly
sensitive environment be significant. Therefore, these classes are considered to apply all instances,
except where the project may impact on an environmental resource of hazardous or critical concern
where designated, precisely mapped, and officially adopted pursuant to law by federal, state, or local
agencies.

(b) Cumulative Impact. All exemptions for these classes are inapplicable when the cumulative impact of
successive projects of the same type in the same place, over time is significant.

(c) Significant Effect. A categorical exemption shall not be used for an activity where there is a
reasonable possibility that the activity will have a significant effect on the environment due to unusual
circumstances.

(d) Scenic Highways. A categorical exemption shall not be used for a project which may result in damage
to scenic resources, including but not limited to, trees, historic buildings, rock outcroppings, or similar
resources, within a highway officially designated as a state scenic highway. This does not apply to
improvements which are required as mitigation by an adopted negative declaration or certified EIR.

(e) Hazardous Waste Sites. A categorical exemption shall not be used for a project located on a site
which is included on any list compiled pursuant to Section 65962.5 of the Government Code.

(f) Historical Resources. A categorical exemption shall not be used for a project which may cause a
substantial adverse change in the significance of a historical resource.

Categorical Exemption Class XI Accessory Structures (Cal. Code Regs.tit. 14 § 15311)
Class 11 projects are described in § 153     construction, or placement of minor structures accessory
to (appurtenant to) existing commercial, industrial, or institutional facilities. The installation of a new
                                                                                        the installation of
structures appurtenant to the school. The proposed project fits the description provided in Cal. Code
Regs. tit. 14 § 15311.



                                                                                                            4
                                                                                                                35
                                               Attachment 1


CEQA Notice of Exemption and Categorical Exemption Memorandum
Bella Vista High School Site Security | Fair Oaks, California
March 25, 2024 | Terracon Project No. NB257045



Categorical Exemption Class XIV Minor Additions to Schools (Cal. Code Regs.tit. 14 § 15314)
Class 14 projects are described in § 15314 as minor additions to existing schools within existing school
grounds where the addition does not increase original student capacity by more than 25% or ten
classrooms, whichever is less. The installation of fencing and gates and relocation of the bike enclosure
would take place entirely within Bella Vista High                   property and would not involve the
addition of any new classrooms, nor would it affect                                The proposed project
fits the description provided in Cal. Code Regs. tit. 14 § 15314.


Summary:
The proposed project would not result in any significant impacts to the environment (please see
Table 1). The activities that make up the proposed project (installation of new fencing and gates,
relocation of bike enclosure) meet both the description of a Class 11 and Class 14-exempt project as
well as the criteria listed in the Exceptions to CEQA Categorical Exemptions. The project area is not
located on a hazard waste site or other environmental feature of critical concern. The proposed project
would not result in a significant impact, nor would it result in a cumulatively considerable contribution
to a significant cumulative impact.

The long-term effects of the project are likely to improve site security. The project site is not in the
vicinity of a Scenic Highway, and the project would not be expected to impact historical resources. No
historic properties are known to exist in the project area; if artifacts were to be found during
construction, work would stop immediately, and a qualified archeologist would be consulted with before
work were to resume.

                                                                                         Bella Vista High
School Site Security Project is Categorically Exempt from CEQA documentation.

Sincerely,
Terracon Consultants, Inc.




Andrea Gonzalez                                          J. Hunter Watkins
Staff Biologist                                          Authorized Project Reviewer

SUBJECT: Andrew Carnegie Middle School Site Security Project CEQA Categorical Exemption

DEPARTMENT: Operations

ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board approve the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA)
Notice of Exemption for the Andrew Carnegie Middle School Site Security Project.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The proposed project is located entirely within Andrew Carnegie Middle School's campus at 5820 Illinois Avenue
(APN's: 261-0311-009-0000, 261-0290-029-0000), in Orangevale, California. The project area spans
approximately 1,441 feet of primarily landscaped and paved areas within boundaries. The project scope includes
the installation of ornamental fencing and double gates, removal of existing chain link fencing, and upgrades to
paths of travel throughout the campus.

As the actions associated with the proposed project are not expected to result in a significant environmental
impact, it is expected that this project is exempt under the Class XI Categorical Exemption (Accessory Structures)
and Class XIV Categorical Exemption (Minor Additions to Schools), as described in the California Code of
Regulations, Title 15, Section 15300 et seq.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. CEQA Notice of Exemption

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                     AGENDA ITEM:                    H.9
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                     MEETING DATE:                04/08/2025

SUBJECT: Mary Deterding Elementary School Site Security Project CEQA Categorical Exemption

DEPARTMENT: Operations

ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board approve the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA)
Notice of Exemption for the Mary Deterding Elementary School Site Security Project.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The proposed project is located entirely within Mary Deterding Elementary School’s campus at 6000 Stanley
Avenue (APN: 273-0070-001-0000), in Carmichael, California. The project area spans approximately 0.16 acres
and 1,493 feet of primarily landscaped and paved areas within the school’s boundaries. The project scope includes
the installation of maintenance gates, accessible mangates, ornamental fencing as well as the removal of trees and
some existing fencing and posts throughout the school campus.

As the actions associated with the proposed project are not expected to result in a significant environmental
impact, it is expected that this project is exempt under the Class XI Categorical Exemption (Accessory Structures)
and Class XIV Categorical Exemption (Minor Additions to Schools), as described in the California Code of
Regulations, Title 15, Section 15300 et seq.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. CEQA Categorical Exemption

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A
PREVIOUS STAFF/BOARD ACTION:
Superintendent's Cabinet: 03/31/2025

FISCAL IMPACT:
N/A

PREPARED BY:                Nicholas Arps, Director, Facilities, Construction and Modernization

APPROVED BY:                Frank Camarda, Chief Operations Officer
                            Melissa Bassanelli, Superintendent of Schools

FROM:           Terracon Consultants, Inc.

DATE:           March 25, 2025

RE:             Mary Deterding Elementary School Site Security Project
                CEQA Categorical Exemption
                Terracon Project No: NB257047



Project Information:
The proposed project is located entirely within Mary Deterding Elementary                     6000
Stanley Avenue (APN: 273-0070-001-0000), in Carmichael, California. The project area spans
approximately 0.16 acres and 1,493 feet of primarily landscaped and paved areas within
boundaries (Exhibit 1). The project scope includes the installation of maintenance gates, accessible
mangates, ornamental fencing as well as the removal of trees and some existing fencing and posts
throughout the school campus.

As the actions associated with the proposed project are not expected to result in a significant
environmental impact, it is expected that this project is exempt under the Class XI Categorical
Exemption (Accessory Structures) and Class XIV Categorical Exemption (Minor Additions to Schools),
as described in the California Code of Regulations, Title 15, Section 15300 et seq.


Legal Setting:
Categorical Exemptions (Cal. Code Regs. tit. 14 § 15300)
Projects that are not expected to result in a significant environmental impact may be Categorically
Exempt from the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) review. As described in Cal. Code Regs.
tit. 14 § 15300, Section 21084 of the Public Resources Code requires these guidelines to include a list
of classes of projects which have been determined not to have a significant effect on the environment
and which shall, therefore, be exempt from the provisions of CEQA. In response to that mandate, the
Secretary for Resources has found that the following classes of projects listed in this article do not have
a significant effect on the environment, and they are declared to be categorically exempt from the
requirement for the preparation of environmental documents.

Like many school-renovation projects (that do not involve additional classrooms or student capacity),
the proposed project is not expected to result in any significant environmental impacts under CEQA.
Table 1 provides an abbreviated CEQA checklist, explaining why the implementation of the proposed
project would not result in any significant environmental impacts.

                         The proposed project would not result in impacts related to scenic vistas, state-
                         listed scenic highways as the nearest scenic location is the California State Route

                         the installation of equipment that would be inconsistent with previous
                         conditions; and would not result in an impact on Aesthetics.

                    The proposed project would not involve agricultural lands or Prime Farmland.
 Forestry Resources

                         The proposed project would not result in the exposure of pollutants or odors to
                         sensitive receptors. Although Sacramento County is in nonattainment status for
                         PM-2.5 (2006) and 8-Hour Ozone (2015) criteria pollutants, the proposed project
                         would not result in a significant net increase of such pollutants, nor would the
                         project conflict with the Sacramento Metropolitan Air Quality Management
 Air Quality

                         Plan (SIP) as the emissions would be associated with the limited use of
                         construction equipment. The equipment required for the installation of fencing
                         and gates and the removal of trees, fencing, and posts utilize smaller engines and
                         would be operated as needed for a limited amount of time.

                         The project area is not expected to provide habitat for federally- or state-listed
                         species, nor would it affect a Habitat Conservation Plan (HCP), Natural
 Biological              Community Conservation Planning (NCCP), or other sensitive biological
 Resources               resources. However, if a nesting bird is found in the trees scheduled for removal
                         during the California nesting bird season (roughly February 1 August 31), a
                         nesting bird survey is recommended.

                         The project does not contain known historic properties and is not suspected to
                         contain archeological artifacts as the general area is previously developed. If
 Cultural Resources      archeological or cultural resources are discovered onsite, work would cease
                         immediately until consultation and approval to continue work was provided by a
                         qualified archeologist.

                         The proposed project would not result in an impact related to the wasteful or
 Energy                  inefficient use of energy since the project will not require the use of equipment
                         with high energy requirements during its operations.

Mary Deterding Elementary School Site Security | Carmichael, California
March 25, 2024 | Terracon Project No. NB257047


                         The school is not located adjacent to a main throughfare and therefore, the
                         proposed project would not have a significant effect on transportation. Further,
 Transportation

                         would not be affected by the work.

 Tribal Cultural         resource as there are no known relationships to the site; however, if resources

                         immediately and both federally and state recognized tribes will be contacted.

 Wildfire

 Mandatory               The proposed project does not have the potential to substantially degrade or
 Findings of             reduce the habitat of a species or impact known resources. The project would
 Significance            not result in a cumulatively considerable contribution to a cumulative impact.


Exceptions (Cal. Code Regs. tit. 14 § 15300.2)
It should be noted that six (6) exceptions are described, which if applicable to a project, would disqualify
the project from the usage of a Categorical Exemption. These exceptions are:

(a) Location. Classes 3, 4, 5, 6, and 11 are qualified by consideration of where the project is to be
located a project that is ordinarily insignificant in its impact on the environment may in a particularly
sensitive environment be significant. Therefore, these classes are considered to apply all instances,
except where the project may impact on an environmental resource of hazardous or critical concern
where designated, precisely mapped, and officially adopted pursuant to law by federal, state, or local
agencies.

(b) Cumulative Impact. All exemptions for these classes are inapplicable when the cumulative impact of
successive projects of the same type in the same place, over time is significant.

(c) Significant Effect. A categorical exemption shall not be used for an activity where there is a
reasonable possibility that the activity will have a significant effect on the environment due to unusual
circumstances.

(d) Scenic Highways. A categorical exemption shall not be used for a project which may result in damage
to scenic resources, including but not limited to, trees, historic buildings, rock outcroppings, or similar
resources, within a highway officially designated as a state scenic highway. This does not apply to
improvements which are required as mitigation by an adopted negative declaration or certified EIR.

(e) Hazardous Waste Sites. A categorical exemption shall not be used for a project located on a site
which is included on any list compiled pursuant to Section 65962.5 of the Government Code.

(f) Historical Resources. A categorical exemption shall not be used for a project which may cause a
substantial adverse change in the significance of a historical resource.




                                                                                                             4
                                                                                                                 51
                                                   Attachment 1


CEQA Notice of Exemption and Categorical Exemption Memorandum
Mary Deterding Elementary School Site Security | Carmichael, California
March 25, 2024 | Terracon Project No. NB257047

Categorical Exemption Class XI Accessory Structures (Cal. Code Regs.tit. 14 § 15311)
Class 11 projects are described in § 153      construction, or placement of minor structures accessory
to (appurtenant to) existing commercial, industrial, or institutional facilities. The installation of a new
                                                                                                 installation
of structures appurtenant to the school. The proposed project fits the description provided in Cal. Code
Regs. tit. 14 § 15311.

Categorical Exemption Class XIV Minor Additions to Schools (Cal. Code Regs.tit. 14 § 15314)
Class 14 projects are described in § 15314 as minor additions to existing schools within existing school
grounds where the addition does not increase original student capacity by more than 25% or ten
classrooms, whichever is less. The project would take place entirely within Mary Deterding Elementary
                 property and would not involve the addition of any new classrooms, nor would it affect
                              The proposed project fits the description provided in Cal. Code Regs. tit.
14 § 15314.


Summary:
The proposed project would not result in any significant impacts to the environment (please see
Table 1). The activities that make up the proposed project (installation of new fencing and gates,
removal of trees and some existing accessory structures) meet both the description of a Class 11 and
Class 14-exempt project as well as the criteria listed in the Exceptions to CEQA Categorical Exemptions.
The project area is not located on a hazard waste site or other environmental feature of critical concern.
The proposed project would not result in a significant impact, nor would it result in a cumulatively
considerable contribution to a significant cumulative impact.

The long-term effects of the project are likely to improve site security. The project site is not in the
vicinity of a Scenic Highway, and the project would not be expected to impact historical resources. No
historic properties are known to exist in the project area; if artifacts were to be found during
construction, work would stop immediately, and a qualified archeologist would be consulted with before
work were to resume.

If nesting birds were to be found in the trees scheduled for removal during the California nesting bird
season (roughly Feb 1 through Aug 31), a nesting bird survey is recommended and the San Juan Unified
School District would be responsible for establishing no-work buffers, as necessary, with the input of
the California Department of Fish and Wildlife (CDFW) before the commencement of tree removal
activities.

                                                                                    Mary Deterding
Elementary School Site Security Project is Categorically Exempt from CEQA documentation.

SUBJECT: Pasadena Avenue Elementary School Site Security Project CEQA Categorical Exemption

DEPARTMENT: Operations

ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board approve the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA)
Notice of Exemption for the Pasadena Avenue Elementary School Site Security Project.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The proposed project is located entirely within Pasadena Avenue Elementary School’s campus at 4330 Pasadena
Avenue (APN’s: 256-0011-001-0000, 256-0011-002-0000, and 256-0011-002-0000), in Sacramento, California.
The project area spans approximately 1.18 acres of primarily landscaped and paved areas within the school’s
boundaries. The project scope includes the installation of new site fencing and gates along the school frontage,
including accessible egress, pedestrian, and maintenance gates.

As the actions associated with the proposed project are not expected to result in a significant environmental
impact, it is expected that this project is exempt under the Class XI Categorical Exemption (Accessory Structures)
and Class XIV Categorical Exemption (Minor Additions to Schools), as described in the California Code of
Regulations, Title 15, Section 15300 et seq.

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                     AGENDA ITEM:                    H.11
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                     MEETING DATE:                04/08/2025

SUBJECT: Pershing Elementary School Site Security Project CEQA Categorical Exemption

DEPARTMENT: Operations

ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board approve the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA)
Notice of Exemption for the Pershing Elementary School Site Security Project.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The proposed project is located entirely within Pershing Elementary School’s campus at 9010 Pershing Avenue
(APN’s: 235-0022-031-0000 and 235-0022-028-0000), in Orangevale, California. The project area spans
approximately 600 square feet and 1,301 feet of primarily landscaped and paved areas within the school’s
boundaries. The project scope includes the installation of double and maintenance gates and fencing as well as the
removal of some existing fencing towards the frontage of the school.

As the actions associated with the proposed project are not expected to result in a significant environmental
impact, it is expected that this project is exempt under the Class XI Categorical Exemption (Accessory Structures)
and Class XIV Categorical Exemption (Minor Additions to Schools), as described in the California Code of
Regulations, Title 15, Section 15300 et seq.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. CEQA Categorical Exemption

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A
PREVIOUS STAFF/BOARD ACTION:
Superintendent's Cabinet: 03/31/2025

FISCAL IMPACT:
N/A

PREPARED BY:                Nicholas Arps, Director, Facilities, Construction and Modernization

APPROVED BY:                Frank Camarda, Chief Operations Officer
                            Melissa Bassanelli, Superintendent of Schools

RE:             Pershing Elementary School Site Security Project
                CEQA Categorical Exemption
                Terracon Project No: NB257048



Project Information:
The proposed project is located entirely within Pershing Elementary                    9010 Pershing
Avenue (APN : 235-0022-031-0000 and 235-0022-028-0000), in Orangevale, California. The project
area spans approximately 600 square feet and 1,301 feet of primarily landscaped and paved areas
within            boundaries (Exhibit 1). The project scope includes the installation of double and
maintenance gates and fencing as well as the removal of some existing fencing towards the frontage of
the school.

As the actions associated with the proposed project are not expected to result in a significant
environmental impact, it is expected that this project is exempt under the Class XI Categorical
Exemption (Accessory Structures) and Class XIV Categorical Exemption (Minor Additions to Schools),
as described in the California Code of Regulations, Title 15, Section 15300 et seq.


Legal Setting:
Categorical Exemptions (Cal. Code Regs. tit. 14 § 15300)
Projects that are not expected to result in a significant environmental impact may be Categorically
Exempt from the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) review. As described in Cal. Code Regs.
tit. 14 § 15300, Section 21084 of the Public Resources Code requires these guidelines to include a list
of classes of projects which have been determined not to have a significant effect on the environment
and which shall, therefore, be exempt from the provisions of CEQA. In response to that mandate, the
Secretary for Resources has found that the following classes of projects listed in this article do not have
a significant effect on the environment, and they are declared to be categorically exempt from the
requirement for the preparation of environmental documents.

Like many school-renovation projects (that do not involve additional classrooms or student capacity),
the proposed project is not expected to result in any significant environmental impacts under CEQA.
Table 1 provides an abbreviated CEQA checklist, explaining why the implementation of the proposed
project would not result in any significant environmental impacts.

                        The proposed project would not result in impacts related to scenic vistas, state-

                        the installation of equipment that would be inconsistent with previous
                        conditions; and would not result in an impact on Aesthetics.

                    The proposed project would not involve agricultural lands or Prime Farmland.

                        sensitive receptors. Although Sacramento County is in nonattainment status for
                        PM-2.5 (2006) and 8-Hour Ozone (2015) criteria pollutants, the proposed project
                        would not result in a significant net increase of such pollutants, nor would the
                        project conflict with the Sacramento Metropolitan Air Quality Management
 Air Quality

                        Plan (SIP) as the emissions would be associated with the limited use of
                        construction equipment. The equipment required for the installation of new
                        gates and fencing and the removal of existing fencing utilize smaller engines and
                        would be operated as needed for a limited amount of time.

                        The project area is not expected to provide habitat for federally- or state-listed
 Biological             species, nor would it affect a Habitat Conservation Plan (HCP), Natural
 Resources              Community Conservation Planning (NCCP), or other sensitive biological
                        resources.

                        The project does not contain known historic properties and is not suspected to
                        contain archeological artifacts as the general area is previously developed. If
 Cultural Resources     archeological or cultural resources are discovered onsite, work would cease
                        immediately until consultation and approval to continue work was provided by a
                        qualified archeologist.

                        The proposed project would not result in an impact related to the wasteful or
 Energy                 inefficient use of energy since the project will not require the use of equipment
                        with high energy requirements during its operations.

                        The proposed project would not result in geological impacts. The project
 Geology and Soils      construction would take place on previously developed and disturbed land and
                        would not result in new construction in unsafe soils.

Exceptions (Cal. Code Regs. tit. 14 § 15300.2)
It should be noted that six (6) exceptions are described, which if applicable to a project, would disqualify
the project from the usage of a Categorical Exemption. These exceptions are:

(a) Location. Classes 3, 4, 5, 6, and 11 are qualified by consideration of where the project is to be
located a project that is ordinarily insignificant in its impact on the environment may in a particularly
sensitive environment be significant. Therefore, these classes are considered to apply all instances,
except where the project may impact on an environmental resource of hazardous or critical concern
where designated, precisely mapped, and officially adopted pursuant to law by federal, state, or local
agencies.

(b) Cumulative Impact. All exemptions for these classes are inapplicable when the cumulative impact of
successive projects of the same type in the same place, over time is significant.

(c) Significant Effect. A categorical exemption shall not be used for an activity where there is a
reasonable possibility that the activity will have a significant effect on the environment due to unusual
circumstances.

(d) Scenic Highways. A categorical exemption shall not be used for a project which may result in damage
to scenic resources, including but not limited to, trees, historic buildings, rock outcroppings, or similar
resources, within a highway officially designated as a state scenic highway. This does not apply to
improvements which are required as mitigation by an adopted negative declaration or certified EIR.

(e) Hazardous Waste Sites. A categorical exemption shall not be used for a project located on a site
which is included on any list compiled pursuant to Section 65962.5 of the Government Code.

(f) Historical Resources. A categorical exemption shall not be used for a project which may cause a
substantial adverse change in the significance of a historical resource.

Categorical Exemption Class XI Accessory Structures (Cal. Code Regs.tit. 14 § 15311)
Class 11 projects are described in § 153     construction, or placement of minor structures accessory
to (appurtenant to) existing commercial, industrial, or institutional facilities. The installation of a new
                                                                                         the installation of
structures appurtenant to the school. The proposed project fits the description provided in Cal. Code
Regs. tit. 14 § 15311.

                                                                                                                68
                                                 Attachment 1


CEQA Notice of Exemption and Categorical Exemption Memorandum
Pershing Elementary School Site Security | Orangevale, California
March 25, 2024 | Terracon Project No. NB257048

Categorical Exemption Class XIV Minor Additions to Schools (Cal. Code Regs.tit. 14 § 15314)
Class 14 projects are described in § 15314 as minor additions to existing schools within existing school
grounds where the addition does not increase original student capacity by more than 25% or ten
classrooms, whichever is less. The project would take place entirely within Pershing Elementary
                 property and would not involve the addition of any new classrooms, nor would it affect
                              The proposed project fits the description provided in Cal. Code Regs. tit.
14 § 15314.


Summary:
The proposed project would not result in any significant impacts to the environment (please see
Table 1). The activities that make up the proposed project (installation of new gates and fencing,
removal of existing fencing) meet both the description of a Class 11 and Class 14-exempt project as
well as the criteria listed in the Exceptions to CEQA Categorical Exemptions. The project area is not
located on a hazard waste site or other environmental feature of critical concern. The proposed project
would not result in a significant impact, nor would it result in a cumulatively considerable contribution
to a significant cumulative impact.

The long-term effects of the project are likely to improve site security. The project site is not in the
vicinity of a Scenic Highway, and the project would not be expected to impact historical resources. No
historic properties are known to exist in the project area; if artifacts were to be found during
construction, work would stop immediately, and a qualified archeologist would be consulted with before
work were to resume.

                                                                                                Pershing
Elementary School Site Security Project is Categorically Exempt from CEQA documentation.

Sincerely,
Terracon Consultants, Inc.

SUBJECT: Whitney Avenue Elementary School Site Security Project CEQA Categorical Exemption

DEPARTMENT: Operations

ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board approve the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA)
Notice of Exemption for the Whitney Avenue Elementary School Site Security Project.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The proposed project is located entirely within Whitney Avenue Elementary School’s campus at 4248 Whitney
Avenue (APN: 255-0196-001-0000), in Sacramento, California. The project area spans approximately 1,534 feet
of primarily landscaped and paved areas within the school’s boundaries. The project scope includes the installation
of double and maintenance gates and ornamental fencing as well as paths of travel upgrades and
removal/replacement of some gates and fencing throughout the school campus.

As the actions associated with the proposed project are not expected to result in a significant environmental
impact, it is expected that this project is exempt under the Class XI Categorical Exemption (Accessory Structures)
and Class XIV Categorical Exemption (Minor Additions to Schools), as described in the California Code of
Regulations, Title 15, Section 15300 et seq.

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                     AGENDA ITEM:                    H.13
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                     MEETING DATE:                04/08/2025

SUBJECT: Albert Schweitzer Elementary School Landscape-Shade Structure Project CEQA Categorical
Exemption

DEPARTMENT: Operations

ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board approve the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA)
Notice of Exemption for the Albert Schweitzer Elementary School Landscape-Shade Structure Project.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The proposed project is located entirely within Albert Schweitzer Elementary School's campus at 4350 Glenridge
Drive (APN: 247-0060-032), in Carmichael, California. The project area spans approximately 0.21 acres of
primarily landscaped and paved areas within boundaries. The project scope includes the demolition and
replacement of existing flatwork and landscaping with new flatwork and landscaping, construction of new canopy
and outdoor learning area, and installation of precast benches.

As the actions associated with the proposed project are not expected to result in a significant environmental
impact, it is expected that this project is exempt under the Class XI Categorical Exemption (Accessory Structures)
and Class XIV Categorical Exemption (Minor Additions to Schools), as described in the California Code of
Regulations, Title 15, Section 15300 et seq.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. CEQA Notice of Exemption

Project Information:
The proposed project is located entirely within Albert Schweitzer Elementary                   4350
Glenridge Drive (APN: 247-0060-032), in Carmichael, California. The project area spans approximately
0.21 acres of primarily landscaped and paved areas within                boundaries (Exhibit 1). The
project scope includes the demolition and replacement of existing flatwork and landscaping with new
flatwork and landscaping, construction of new canopy and outdoor learning area, and installation of
precast benches.

As the actions associated with the proposed project are not expected to result in a significant
environmental impact, it is expected that this project is exempt under the Class XI Categorical
Exemption (Accessory Structures) and Class XIV Categorical Exemption (Minor Additions to Schools),
as described in the California Code of Regulations, Title 15, Section 15300 et seq.


Legal Setting:
Categorical Exemptions (Cal. Code Regs. tit. 14 § 15300)
Projects that are not expected to result in a significant environmental impact may be Categorically
Exempt from the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA) review. As described in Cal. Code Regs.
tit. 14 § 15300, Section 21084 of the Public Resources Code requires these guidelines to include a list
of classes of projects which have been determined not to have a significant effect on the environment
and which shall, therefore, be exempt from the provisions of CEQA. In response to that mandate, the
Secretary for Resources has found that the following classes of projects listed in this article do not have
a significant effect on the environment, and they are declared to be categorically exempt from the
requirement for the preparation of environmental documents.

Like many school-renovation projects (that do not involve additional classrooms or student capacity),
the proposed project is not expected to result in any significant environmental impacts under CEQA.
Table 1 provides an abbreviated CEQA checklist, explaining why the implementation of the proposed
project would not result in any significant environmental impacts.

Exceptions (Cal. Code Regs. tit. 14 § 15300.2)
It should be noted that six (6) exceptions are described, which if applicable to a project, would disqualify
the project from the usage of a Categorical Exemption. These exceptions are:

(a) Location. Classes 3, 4, 5, 6, and 11 are qualified by consideration of where the project is to be
located a project that is ordinarily insignificant in its impact on the environment may in a particularly
sensitive environment be significant. Therefore, these classes are considered to apply all instances,
except where the project may impact on an environmental resource of hazardous or critical concern
where designated, precisely mapped, and officially adopted pursuant to law by federal, state, or local
agencies.

(b) Cumulative Impact. All exemptions for these classes are inapplicable when the cumulative impact of
successive projects of the same type in the same place, over time is significant.

(c) Significant Effect. A categorical exemption shall not be used for an activity where there is a
reasonable possibility that the activity will have a significant effect on the environment due to unusual
circumstances.

(d) Scenic Highways. A categorical exemption shall not be used for a project which may result in damage
to scenic resources, including but not limited to, trees, historic buildings, rock outcroppings, or similar
resources, within a highway officially designated as a state scenic highway. This does not apply to
improvements which are required as mitigation by an adopted negative declaration or certified EIR.

(e) Hazardous Waste Sites. A categorical exemption shall not be used for a project located on a site
which is included on any list compiled pursuant to Section 65962.5 of the Government Code.

(f) Historical Resources. A categorical exemption shall not be used for a project which may cause a
substantial adverse change in the significance of a historical resource.

CEQA Notice of Exemption and Categorical Exemption Memorandum
Albert Schweitzer Elementary School Landscape-Shade Structure | Carmichael, California

Categorical Exemption Class XI Accessory Structures (Cal. Code Regs.tit. 14 § 15311)
Class 11 projects are described in § 15311      construction, or placement of minor structures accessory
to (appurtenant to) existing commercial, industrial, or institutional facilities. The installation of a new
                                                                                                qualifies as
installing structures appurtenant to the school. The proposed project fits the description provided in Cal.
Code Regs. tit. 14 § 15311.

Categorical Exemption Class XIV Minor Additions to Schools (Cal. Code Regs.tit. 14 § 15314)
Class 14 projects are described in § 15314 as minor additions to existing schools within existing school
grounds where the addition does not increase original student capacity by more than 25% or ten
classrooms, whichever is less. The replacement of flatwork and landscaping in addition to the
installation of a new canopy and benches would take place entirely within Albert Schweitzer Elementary
                   property. It would not involve the addition of any new classrooms, nor would it affect
                                The proposed project fits the description provided in Cal. Code Regs. tit.
14 § 15314.


Summary:
The proposed project would not result in any significant impacts to the environment (please see
Table 1). The activities that make up the proposed project (demolition and replacement of flatwork and
landscaping, installation of canopy and benches) meet both the description of a Class 11 and Class 14-
exempt project as well as the criteria listed in the Exceptions to CEQA Categorical Exemptions. The
project area is not located on a hazard waste site or other environmental feature of critical concern. The
proposed project would not result in a significant impact, nor would it result in a cumulatively
considerable contribution to a significant cumulative impact.

The long-term effects of the project are likely to improve the recreational and outdoor learning
opportunities on campus. The project site is not in the vicinity of a Scenic Highway, and the project
would not be expected to impact historical resources. No historic properties are known to exist in the
project area; if artifacts were to be found during construction, work would stop immediately, and a
qualified archeologist would be consulted with before work were to resume.

documentation.

BOARD OF EDUCATION

SUBJECT: San Juan High School Athletic Facility Improvement Project CEQA Categorical Exemption

DEPARTMENT: Operations

ACTION REQUESTED:
The superintendent is recommending that the board approve the California Environmental Quality Act (CEQA)
Notice of Exemption for the San Juan High School Athletic Facility Improvement Project.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The proposed project is located entirely within San Juan High School’s campus at 7551 Greenback Lane (APN:
243-0170-006), in Citrus Heights, California. The project area spans approximately 6.7 acres of a primarily
developed and landscaped area within the school’s boundaries. The project scope includes the demolition of the
preexisting grass field, installation of synthetic turf field, running track, and associated infrastructure (hardscape,
fencing, drinking fountains, utilities, etc.) and additions/site furnishings that accommodate multiple sports, as well
as a new restroom, concession building, and ticket booth.

As the actions associated with the proposed project are not expected to result in a significant environmental
impact, it is expected that this project is exempt under the Class II Categorical Exemption (Replacement or
Reconstruction) and Class XIV Categorical Exemption (Minor Additions to Schools), as described in the
California Code of Regulations, Title 14, Section 15300 et seq.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. CEQA Categorical Exemption

Exceptions (Cal. Code Regs. tit. 14 § 15300.2)
It should be noted that six (6) exceptions are described, which if applicable to a project, would disqualify
the project from the usage of a Categorical Exemption. These exceptions are:

(a) Location. Classes 3, 4, 5, 6, and 11 are qualified by consideration of where the project is to be
located a project that is ordinarily insignificant in its impact on the environment may in a particularly
sensitive environment be significant. Therefore, these classes are considered to apply all instances,
except where the project may impact on an environmental resource of hazardous or critical concern
where designated, precisely mapped, and officially adopted pursuant to law by federal, state, or local
agencies.

(b) Cumulative Impact. All exemptions for these classes are inapplicable when the cumulative impact of
successive projects of the same type in the same place, over time is significant.

(c) Significant Effect. A categorical exemption shall not be used for an activity where there is a
reasonable possibility that the activity will have a significant effect on the environment due to unusual
circumstances.

(d) Scenic Highways. A categorical exemption shall not be used for a project which may result in damage
to scenic resources, including but not limited to, trees, historic buildings, rock outcroppings, or similar
resources, within a highway officially designated as a state scenic highway. This does not apply to
improvements which are required as mitigation by an adopted negative declaration or certified EIR.

which is included on any list compiled pursuant to Section 65962.5 of the Government Code.

substantial adverse change in the significance of a historical resource.
