                                                                                                                  92
                                                   Attachment 1
CEQA Categorical Exemption Memorandum
San Juan High School Athletic Facility Improvement Project | Citrus Heights, California
March 12, 2025 | Terracon Project No. NB257032



Categorical Exemption Class II         Replacement or Reconstruction (Cal. Code Regs.tit. 14 §
15302)
Class 2 projects are described in § 15302       replacement or reconstruction of existing structures and
facilities where the new structure will be located on the same site as the structure replaced and will
have substantially the same purpose and capacity as the structure replaced. The proposed project
includes the reconstruction of a new athletic facility on San Juan High          campus, which fits the
description provided in Cal. Code Regs. tit. 14 § 15302.

Categorical Exemption Class XIV Minor Additions to Schools (Cal. Code Regs.tit. 14 § 15314)
Class 14 projects are described in § 15314 as minor additions to existing schools within existing school
grounds where the addition does not increase original student capacity by more than 25% or ten
classrooms, whichever is less. The reconstruction and installation of a new athletic facility and
associated infrastructure/furnishings would take place entirely within San Juan High              xisting
property and would not involve the addition of new classrooms, nor would it increase
capacity. The proposed project fits the description provided in Cal. Code Regs. tit. 14 § 15314.


Summary:
The proposed project would not result in any significant impacts to the environment (please see
Table 1). The activities that make up the proposed project (demolition and reconstruction of a new
athletic facility) meet both the descriptions of a Class 2 and Class 14-exempt project as well as the
criteria listed in the Exceptions to CEQA Categorical Exemptions. The project area is not located on a
hazard waste site or other environmental feature of critical concern. The proposed project would not
result in a significant impact, nor would it result in a cumulatively considerable contribution to a
significant cumulative impact.

The long-term effects of the project will likely improve athletic and recreational opportunities for the
students. The project site is not in the vicinity of a Scenic Highway, and the project would not be
expected to impact historical resources. No historic properties are known to exist in the project area; if
artifacts were to be found during construction, work would stop immediately, and a qualified archeologist
would be consulted with before work were to resume.

If nesting birds were to be found in trees scheduled for removal during the California nesting bird season
(roughly Feb 1 through Aug 31), a nesting bird survey is recommended and the San Juan Unified School
District would be responsible for establishing no-work buffers, as necessary, with the input of the
California Department of Fish and Wildlife (CDFW) before the commencement of tree removal activities.

                                                                                     San Juan High
School Athletic Facility Improvement Project is Categorically Exempt from CEQA documentation.

    RESOLUTION BEFORE THE SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT
   BOARD OF EDUCATION APPROVING LEASE AMENDMENT #1 FOR THE
GATEWAY INTERNATIONAL SCHOOL (WINTERSTEIN SITE) PORTABLE, FIELD
      MODIFACATION, TK/KINDER WING, AND SHADE STRUCTURE
                  SJUSD PROJECT #153-9568-24CIP

                                   RESOLUTION NO. 4202

WHEREAS, sections 17406 of the Education Code authorize school districts, including the San
Juan Unified School District (“District”), to use the lease-leaseback procurement process;

WHEREAS, the District Board of Education (“Board”) previously approved the award of the
Site Lease and Facilities Lease to Robert A. Bothman Inc. dba Robert A. Bothman Construction
for this Project, including preconstruction services in the amount of $187,378.00; and

WHEREAS, the approval of the Facilities Lease authorized only preconstruction services to be
performed; no construction services were approved to commence; and no construction services
have commenced; and

WHEREAS, Robert A. Bothman Construction has completed the preconstruction services for
Increment #1 – Classroom Portables, Restroom Portable, and Field Improvements of the Project,
including development of the Total Base Rent for this Increment, and has provided the District
with objectively verifiable information and a written rationale for this Total Base Rent, together
with supporting documents;

WHEREAS, the District has carefully considered the information supporting the Total Base
Rent for Increment #1 of the Project; and

WHEREAS, the Division of the State Architect (“DSA”) approval is required and received for
work associated with Increment #1 of the Project.

NOW, THEREFORE, the San Juan Unified School District Board of Education does hereby
resolve as follows:

Section 1. The foregoing recitals are hereby adopted as true and correct.

Section 2. The Board approves the Total Base Rent in the amount of $2,993,713.00 for
Increment #1, authorizes the issuance of Lease Amendment #1 to the Facilities Lease, and
authorizes District staff to issue a notice to proceed with construction of Increment #1.

Net Change by Amendment #1                                                         $2,993,713.00
Revised Total Base Rent                                                            $2,993,713.00

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                       AGENDA ITEM:                   J.1
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                       MEETING DATE:              04/08/2025

SUBJECT: College and Career Readiness Update - Part 2 (Schnepp) - 7:25 p.m.

DEPARTMENT: Teaching and Learning

ACTION REQUESTED:
Report: The superintendent is recommending that the board receive the report on college and career readiness.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The purpose of this report is to update the board on San Juan Unified's progress related to college and career
readiness for all students. College and career readiness has been identified as one of the seven indicators on the
California School Dashboard. College and Career Indicators (CCI) represent the percentage of high school
graduates who leave high school prepared for college or a career. Over the last few years, San Juan Unified has
been working to increase college and career readiness in both academic and social/emotional areas and will
continue to create and expand opportunities for all students.

On October 8, 2024, the board received a presentation (part 1) on two components of college and career indicators:
Career Technical Education (CTE) pathways and Dual Enrollment (DE), or college and credit courses.

Part 2 of this series will provide additional information and data on the College and Career Indicators (CCI) with
an emphasis on A-G Completion and Advanced Placement (AP). In addition, information will be provided on
Naviance, a college and career readiness planning platform, with an emphasis on the scope and sequence our K-12
schools are using to promote and educate all students on college and career access and opportunities.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. College Career Readiness - Part 2 Presentation
2. College and Career Indicators
3. Dashboard CCI Measures Report 2024
4. College and Career Readiness - Part 1 Presentation from 10/8/2024 board meeting

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A

PREVIOUS STAFF/BOARD ACTION:
Superintendent's Cabinet: 03/31/2025

N/A

    What is the College
    Career Indicator (CCI)?

•   CCI is one of several state indicators the
    California Department of Education (CDE)
    reports on the Dashboard
•   CCI represents the percentage of high
    school graduates who leave high school
    prepared for college or a career
•   CCI is designed to encourage high
    schools to provide all students with a
    rigorous broad course of study that             San Juan Unified is in the Green for College/Career
    prepares them for postsecondary
    success

        What is CCI "Prepared"?
         A student earns "Prepared" on the
         California Dashboard's College/Career
         Indicator (CCI) by completing academic
         and/or career pathways. Examples
         include combinations of the below
         multiple measures:

         • Passing Advanced Placement (AP) or
           International Baccalaureate (IB) exams
         • Completing a-g coursework with a C or
           better
         • Finishing a Career Technical Education
           (CTE) pathway
         • Earning college credits through dual
           enrollment

                                                                                Attachment 2


College/Career Indicator (CCI):
Measures of Career Readiness                                     2024 Dashboard Toolkit


The CCI shows how well local educational agencies (LEAs) and schools are preparing high school
students for success after graduation, whether in postsecondary education or in a career. For
this reason, the CCI consists of both college- and career-readiness measures. This flyer contains
the career-readiness measures. For college-readiness measures, please access the
California Department of Education UNIVERSITY
                                     (CDE) CCI: Measures of College Readiness document.
Career readiness means completing rigorous coursework and engaging in learning experiences
that are designed to prepare students for the workforce. Several measures have been approved by
the State Board of Education as indicating career readiness, as shown below. For each measure,
specific criteria are used to determine whether a student is “Prepared” or “Approaching Prepared.”




Prepared
Graduates classified as Prepared must meet at least one of the following criteria:
  •   Leadership/Military Science
      Complete two years of Leadership/Military Science and receive a score of Level 3 or higher in
      one subject area on both English language arts/literacy (ELA) and mathematics and a score
      of Level 2 “Standard Nearly Met” or higher in the other
  •   Career Technical Education (CTE) Pathway
      Complete a CTE Pathway with a grade of C− or better in the capstone course and meet one
      of the additional criteria below:
      − Smarter Balanced Summative Assessments: receive a score of Level 3 or higher in one
         subject area (ELA or mathematics) and a score of Level 2 or higher in the other
      − Complete one semester, two quarters, or two trimesters of College Credit Courses, outside
         of the completed CTE Pathway, with a grade of C− or better in academic/CTE subjects
         where college credits are awarded for each course
  •   Registered Pre-Apprenticeship
      Complete a registered pre-apprenticeship


                                                                                                      116
CCI: Measures of Career Readiness, continued



  •   State and Federal Job Programs (Dashboard Alternative School Status [DASS] schools
      only)
      Complete one semester, two quarters, or two trimesters of a CTE course with a C− or
      better and complete one of the following programs: Workforce Innovation and Opportunity
      Act (WIOA), Job Corps, YouthBuild, California Conservation Corps (CCC), or Regional
      Occupational Centers and Programs (ROCP)
  •   Transition Classroom and Work-Based Learning Experiences (available only to
      students with individualized education programs [IEPs] who earn a Special Education
      Certificate of Completion)
      Complete at least 100 hours of work experience and the equivalent of four semester courses
      of college and career exploration/preparation designed to prepare a student with an IEP for
      employment and independent living

Approaching Prepared
Graduates classified as Approaching Prepared must meet at least one of the following criteria:
  •   Leadership/Military Science
      Complete two years of Leadership/Military Science
  •   CTE Pathway
      Complete a CTE Pathway with a grade of C− or better in the capstone course
  •   State and Federal Job Programs (DASS schools only)
      Complete one of the programs (i.e., WIOA, Job Corps, YouthBuild, CCC, or ROCP)
  •   Transition Classroom or Work-Based Learning Experiences (available only to students
      with IEPs who earn a Special Education Certificate of Completion)
      Complete at least 100 hours of work experience or the equivalent of four semester courses
      of college and career exploration/preparation designed to prepare a student with an IEP for
      employment and independent living




For more information, visit the CDE California School Dashboard and System
of Support web page.
Contact the Analysis, Measurement, and Accountability Reporting Division by
email at dashboard@cde.ca.gov.
                                                                                      October 2024
                                                                                                     117
College/Career Indicator (CCI):
Measures of College Readiness                                    2024 Dashboard Toolkit


The CCI shows how well local educational agencies (LEAs) and schools are preparing high school
students for success after graduation, whether in postsecondary education or in a career. For
this reason, the CCI consists of both college- and career-readiness measures. This flyer contains
the college-readiness measures. For career-readiness measures, please access the
California Department of Education (CDE) CCI: Measures of Career Readiness document.
College readiness means completing rigorous coursework, passing challenging exams, or receiving
a state seal. Several measures have been approved by the State Board of Education as indicating
college readiness, as shown below. For each measure, specific criteria are used to determine
whether a student is “Prepared” or “Approaching Prepared.”




Prepared
Graduates classified as Prepared must meet at least one of the following criteria:
 • Smarter Balanced Summative Assessments
   Receive a score of Level 3 “Standard Met” or higher on both English language arts/literacy
   (ELA) and mathematics
 • Advanced Placement (AP) Exams
   Receive a score of 3 or higher on two AP exams
 • International Baccalaureate (IB) Exams
   Receive a score of 4 or higher on two IB exams
 • College Credit Courses
   Complete two semesters, three quarters, or three trimesters of college coursework within high
   school with a grade of C− or better in academic/Career Technical Education (CTE) subjects
   where college credits are awarded
 • State Seal of Biliteracy (SSB)
   Receive the SSB and a score of Level 3 or higher in ELA on the Smarter Balanced Summative
   Assessments



                                                                                                    118
CCI: Measures of College Readiness, continued



 • University of California (UC) and California State University (CSU) Requirements
   Meet all A-G requirements for admission to a UC or CSU school and meet one of the additional
   criteria below:
     – Smarter Balanced Summative Assessments: receive a score of Level 3 or higher in one
       subject area (ELA or mathematics) and a score of Level 2 in the other area
     – Complete one semester, two quarters, or two trimesters of College Credit Courses within
       high school with a grade of C− or better in academic/CTE subjects where college credits are
       awarded for each course
     – Receive a score of 3 on one AP exam or score 4 on one IB exam
     – Complete a CTE Pathway

Approaching Prepared
Graduates classified as Approaching Prepared must meet at least one of the following criteria:
 • Smarter Balanced Summative Assessments
   Receive a score of Level 2 “Standard Nearly Met” on both ELA and mathematics
 • College Credit Courses
   Complete one semester, two quarters, or two trimesters of college coursework within high
   school with a grade of C− or better in academic/CTE subjects where college credits are
   awarded
 • UC and CSU Requirements
   Meet all A-G requirements for admission to a UC or CSU school




For more information, visit the CDE California School Dashboard and System
of Support web page.
Contact the Analysis, Measurement, and Accountability Reporting Division by
email at dashboard@cde.ca.gov.
                                                                                     November 2024 119
                                                                                                                       Attachment 3
College/Career Levels and Measures Report & Data - 2024

San Juan Unified (Sacramento County, CA)

* https://www6.cde.ca.gov/californiamodel/ccireport?&year=2024&cdcode=3467447&scode=&reporttype=schools



Overview:
The College/Career Indicator (CCI) is based on students in the combined four- and five-year graduation rate (i.e., current four-year
graduation cohort plus fifth year graduates from prior cohort). It includes both college and career measures to evaluate how well districts
and schools are preparing students for success after high school.

This report displays the number and percentage of graduates who met each of the measures in the CCI Prepared and Approaching Prepared
Levels. Students can meet more than one measure in each CCI level. As a result, the tables contain duplicative student counts.




 * The California Department of Education Dashboard Report link
                                                                                                                                              120
121
How Students Met Prepared


The table below displays the number and percent of students assigned to Prepared Levels for each CCI measure by student group. The four
shades (or levels) represent four percentile ranges (as shown in the legend below) to help identify which measures have a high percentage
(darker shade) or low percentage (lighter shade) of students meeting the criteria. Students can meet more than one measure. As a result, the
tables contain duplicative counts.

Calculation Formula Example:
For All Students: (Number of CTE Prepared Students) divided by (Total Number of Prepared Students)
For Student Groups: (Number of English learners who met CTE Prepared) divided by (Total Number of Prepared English learners)

Career Technical Education
Career and Technical Education (CTE) is a type of education that
prepares students for careers by providing them with academic,
technical, and real-world skills and knowledge. .

 College Credit Course/Dual Enrollment
Dual enrollment enables high school students to take college
courses, taught by college professors, at a high school campus.
These courses not only count towards a high school diploma but
also allow students to get a head start on higher post-secondary
education goals.

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                     AGENDA ITEM:                     J.2
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                     MEETING DATE:                04/08/2025

SUBJECT: New High School Courses for 2025-2026 (Slavensky) - 7:45 p.m.

DEPARTMENT: Teaching and Learning

ACTION REQUESTED:
Action: The superintendent is recommending that the board approve the new proposed high school courses.
(Discussed: 03/25/2025).

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
The proposed high school courses of study listed below are designed to ensure student choice and instructional
alignment with the Strategic Plan, Local Control and Accountability Plan (LCAP), and California’s State
Standards. The proposed courses of study provide a high level of rigor, deeper opportunities for study, and promote
college and career readiness. New high school courses are available for review in the superintendent's office. The
Curriculum, Standards, Instructional and Student Services Committee reviewed and discussed these proposed new
courses at their meeting on March 19, 2025.

Courses:
     Science:
            The Science of Food
     Math:
            Financial Math
            Traffic Analysis and Engineering
     English
            Middle Years Programme (MYP) 4 Language and Literature: Ethnic Studies
            English 9: Ethnic Studies
     Social Studies:
            Advanced Placement (AP) African American Studies
            Chicano Studies
            Middle Years Programme (MYP) 5 United States History and Ethnic Studies
     Art:
            Music and Ethnic Studies
            Animation I: Introduction to Animation
            Animation II: Intermediate
            Animation III: Advanced
     College Preparatory Electives:
            Math Modeling
            Podcasting and Storytelling
            Science Olympiad
            Principles of Athletic Performance
            English Language Development (ELD) IV
            International Baccalaureate Career-related Programme (IBCP) 2 Personal and Professional Skills
     Adult Education:
            Job Readiness
ATTACHMENT(S):
1. New Course Rationale

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
Curriculum, Standards, Instructional & Student Services Committee: 03/19/2025 (discussion & action)

PREVIOUS STAFF/BOARD ACTION:
Superintendent's Cabinet: 03/17/2025, 03/31/2025


                                                                                                                      133
Board of Education: 03/25/2025 (discussion)
FISCAL IMPACT:
N/A

PREPARED BY:               Nicole Kukral, Director, Professional Learning and Curriculum Innovation

APPROVED BY:               Amy L. Slavensky, Ph.D., Interim Deputy Superintendent, Schools & Student Support
                           Melissa Bassanelli, Superintendent of Schools




                                                                                                               134
                               San Juan Unified School District
                            New High School Courses for 2025-2026
                                    Rationale/Background




Advanced Placement (AP) African American Studies (A-G):
AP African American Studies is an interdisciplinary course that examines the diversity of African American
experiences through direct encounters with varied sources. Students explore key topics that extend from
early African kingdoms to the ongoing challenges and achievements of the contemporary moment. Given
the interdisciplinary character of African American Studies, students in the course will develop skills across
multiple fields, with an emphasis on developing historical, literary, visual, and data analysis skills. This
course foregrounds a study of the diversity of Black communities in the United States within the broader
context of Africa and the African diaspora. (“g”) (District)

Animation I (An Introduction to Animation) (A-G):
This course introduces students to the fundamentals of animation and computer graphics. Students will
learn basic concepts, methods, and techniques through hands-on experiences and projects directly related
to the field of animation and computer graphics. The curriculum is geared toward individuals who wish to
use and develop their creative expression skills, in conjunction with professional-level computer software
techniques, to create multimedia art. This course is especially for students who are interested in fine art
communication, film. drama, computer animation, and/or graphic design. Careers in art and animation will
be explored. Furthermore, as the first course in the CTE Animation Pathway, students will focus on basic
visual problem solving, basic storytelling, digital fundamentals, basic character and layout design, basic
animation, basic storyboarding, and basic production. (“f”) (Del Campo)

Animation II (Intermediate) (A-G):
This course will serve as the concentrator course for the Animation pathway. Students will build on
foundational artistic and technical animation skills learned from the introductory course with an emphasis
on the principles of animation, developing draftsmanship, and professional production techniques. In
addition, students will learn to create and maintain a portfolio that showcases their body of work. Students
will explore the career options and opportunities by examining the variety of jobs in the Arts Media and
Entertainment (AME) job sector. By the end of this course, students will have successfully completed
multiple individual and group projects and will be ready to work on large productions in the capstone
course. Furthermore, as the second course in the CTE Animation Pathway, students will focus on
intermediate visual problem solving, intermediate storytelling, animation fundamentals, intermediate
animation, intermediate character and layout design, personal portfolio/demo reel and resume, intermediate
storyboarding and production. (“f”) (Del Campo)

Animation III (Advanced) (A-G):
Advanced Animation is the capstone course in a high school course series (Animation I, Animation II and/or
Advanced Cinema/Film/Video Productions) to complete a comprehensive animation and multimedia
design training. This capstone course provides a hands-on studio environment for in-depth exploration of
advanced digital animation production techniques. This is a project-based course focusing on the use of
current industry software in digital animation. Units will be designed around the creation of projects for
students to design, build, create or perform. To be successful in arts-related careers, self-discipline is a
requirement. This project-based learning environment aligns with industry standards that require time-
management skills, the ability to meet strict deadlines, knowledge of ever-changing technology and
interpersonal skills. Furthermore, as the capstone course in the CTE Animation Pathway, students will focus
on ideas and pitches, visual research, development and design, character design, storyboard production,
layout, sound and story, rough and key animation, polish animation, digital portfolio development.
(“f”) (Del Campo)




                                                                                                                 135
Chicano Studies (A-G):
This course has been designed as a survey course of the Chicano Mexican people prior to the Spanish
colonization of the Americas to the present century. This course will provide an overview of culture,
religion, education, economics, immigration and civil rights. This course will examine the Spanish, Indian,
Mexican contributions to the development of Western United States. Students will examine how the social
ideas of race and class influence social behavior and self-identity of the people of Mexican descent and how
it reflects with the demographics of our community. (“a”) (San Juan)

English 9: Ethnic Studies (A-G):
Students in this course will read and analyze a broad range of nonfiction and fiction selections, deepening
their awareness of how language works in effectively communicating ideas. Through texts that may
potentially range from essays, speeches, articles, and historical documents to novels, plays, poetry, and
short stories, students analyze the use of elements of literature and nonfiction using the Ethnic Studies
framework and a literature lens. As they develop their writing skills and respond to claims, students learn
to formulate arguments and use textual evidence to support their position. To improve their listening,
speaking, and civic engagement skills students engage with a variety of media types through which they
analyze and synthesize information, discuss material, create presentations, and share their work in a
community setting. Students build their writing and speaking skills in potential activities such as journal
responses, discussions, frequent free-response exercises, essays, and presentations, while learning to
communicate clearly and credibly in narrative, argumentative and expository styles. Additionally, this
course aims to educate students to be politically, socially, and economically conscious about their personal
connections to local and global narratives and histories through the interdisciplinary lens of Ethnic Studies.
By studying the histories of race, indigeneity, ancestry, national origin, diaspora, racism, hegemony,
ethnicity, and culture, students will develop respect and empathy for individuals, groups of people locally,
nationally, and globally. (“b”) (District)

English Language Development (ELD) IV (A-G):
The ELD IV course is designed to develop academic language proficiency in English while simultaneously
working on grade level academic content in order to reclassify. It also attends to the particular English
development needs of long-term English learners to promote high levels of English language proficiency.
The course will focus on reading, writing, speaking, and listening of various informational text as well as
produce a student publication of topics important and appropriate to students. (“g”) (District)

Financial Math (A-G):
This course combines algebraic concepts with practical financial applications. Students will learn to apply
math skills to real-world financial situations, including budgeting, saving, investing, credit management,
and financial decision-making. The course emphasizes problem-solving, data interpretation, and financial
literacy to help students make informed decisions about their financial futures. (“c”) (District)

International Baccalaureate Career-related Programme (IBCP) 2: Personal and Professional Skills (A-G):
The Personal and Professional Skills course is designed for students to develop attitudes, skills and
strategies to be applied to personal and professional situations and contexts now and in the future. In this
course the emphasis is on skills development for the workplace, as these are transferable and can be applied
in a range of situations. Other qualities the course should encourage include responsibility, perseverance,
resilience, self-esteem, and academic honesty. (“g”) (Mira Loma)

Job Readiness (Adult Education)
Job Readiness four week-long class is in-person with weekly online appointments to check in and answer
questions. Students learn about how to write a resume, cover letter, basic computer skills, Google review,
Internet basics, thank you letters, references sheet, learn skills in interviewing, filling out a job application,
as well as overcoming barriers to employment, and reviewing labor market information. Students will
analyze their interests related to the job field and practice interviewing at the completion of the class.
(Adult Education)




                                                                                                                     136
Mathematical Modeling (A-G):
The course engages students in developing the Standards of Mathematical Practice through an interactive
curriculum that emphasizes critical thinking, collaboration, and active problem solving. Students will
deepen their understanding of key Integrated Math 1 concepts while exploring foundational topics from
Integrated Math 2. (“g”) (District)

Middle Years Programme (MYP) 4 Language and Literature: Ethnic Studies (A-G):
Students in this course will read and analyze a broad range of nonfiction and fiction selections, deepening
their awareness of how language works in effectively communicating ideas. Through texts that may
potentially range from essays, speeches, articles, and historical documents to novels, plays, poetry, and
short stories, students analyze the use of elements of literature and nonfiction using the Ethnic Studies
framework and a literature lens. As they develop their writing skills and respond to claims, students learn
to formulate arguments and use textual evidence to support their position. To improve their listening,
speaking, and civic engagement skills students engage with a variety of media types through which they
analyze and synthesize information, discuss material, create presentations, and share their work in a
community setting. Students build their writing and speaking skills in potential activities such as journal
responses, discussions, frequent free-response exercises, essays, and presentations, while learning to
communicate clearly and credibly in narrative, argumentative and expository styles. Students will explore
key and related concepts through MYP global contexts: identities and relationships, orientation in space
and time, personal and cultural expression, scientific and technical innovation, globalization and
sustainability, fairness and development. Additionally, this course aims to educate students to be politically,
socially, and economically conscious about their personal connections to local and global narratives and
histories through the interdisciplinary lens of Ethnic Studies. By studying the histories of race, indigeneity,
ancestry, national origin, diaspora, racism, hegemony, ethnicity, and culture, students will develop respect
and empathy for individuals, groups of people locally, nationally, and globally. (“b”) (Mira Loma)

Middle Years Programme (MYP) 5 United States History: Ethnic Studies (A-G):
MYP Individuals and Societies 5 (Honors) United States History with Ethnic Studies is a survey course of
American history from the 1870s to the present day. This survey embeds the Ethnic Studies approaches to
focus on examining American historical viewpoints on race, ethnicity, culture, and power to help students
develop a broader understanding of the history of the American people. The themes of the course are as
outlined: identity and culture, systems of power, history and movements, and social movements and equity.
Each unit in this course will follow the list of key outcomes provided by the California History-Social
Science Framework for ethnic studies: pursuit of justice and equity; working toward greater inclusivity;
furthering self-understanding; developing a better understanding of others; recognizing intersectionality;
promoting self-empowerment for civic engagement; supporting a community focus; and developing
interpersonal communication. (“a”) (Mira Loma)

Music and Ethnic Studies (A-G):
In this Music and Ethnic Studies course, students will develop and cultivate respect, empathy, and solidarity
with historically marginalized groups of people reflected in our local demographics (Native Americans,
African Americans, Latino/a/x Americans, Asian, South Asian and Pacific Islander Americans, Middle
Eastern and others) through the study of their music. This may include, but not limited to, the study of
musical origins, influence in American musical landscape, social movements, hands on music making, and
connections with other art forms. (“f”) (Bella Vista)




                                                                                                                  137
Podcasting and Storytelling (A-G):
Podcasting and Storytelling is a semester course that will explore the medium of podcasting, specifically in
the context of narrative storytelling. The foundation of the course is an exploration into the elements of
storytelling, focusing on the rhetorical choices that a writer/producer must consider (structure, diction,
evidence, audience, voice and tone). Students will begin the semester with a teacher-selected core reading
list that allows them to explore and build awareness of the art of storytelling. As the semester progresses,
students will work in collaborative groups with the instructor to create their own reading lists, which will
be inquiry-based and will inform them more about the subject that they choose for their own podcast.
Students will produce three shorter podcasts to practice particular elements of podcasting. The fourth
podcast, the capstone project for this class, is the creation of an original podcast that incorporates student
research, interviews, and original writing, and that will be produced and published for our school audience.
(“g”) (Del Campo)

Principles of Athletic Performance (A-G):
This course may be conducted in both classroom and physical activity settings. The physical activity portion
will emphasize personal fitness and cover topics such as strength training, cardiovascular training, and team
sports. Principles of Athletic Performance will educate students on fundamental concepts of health,
wellness, nutrition, fitness, and team sport participation. Students will be able to develop analytical thinking
and research the different ways that they can improve their muscle endurance and nutrition for their health
and activity level. (“g”) (Del Campo)

Science Olympiad (A-G):
The Science Olympiad course teaches a hands-on diverse STEM program where students work individually,
and in teams, to prepare for and participate in various science-based events. Encompassing topics like
biology, chemistry, physics, engineering, and earth science; students foster critical thinking, collaboration,
and a deeper understanding of scientific concepts by building projects, solving problems, and demonstrating
their knowledge through practical applications. (“g”) (Mira Loma)

The Science of Food (A-G):
Food Science is the study of the physical, biological and chemical makeup of food along with the
processing, preservation, and development of food products. Through laboratory activities, class
discussions, research projects, and supplemental lectures, students will apply chemistry, microbiology, and
biochemistry principles as they pertain to the food science industry. The topics in this class include the
chemical breakdown of food (micronutrients and macronutrients), processing and preservation of food,
sensory science, and food product development. (“d”) (Interdisciplinary Science) (Mira Loma)

Traffic Analysis and Engineering (A-G):
The course spans the full range of key areas from characteristics of the transportation system, analysis of
flow and capacity, traffic operations, traffic control devices, pedestrian/bicycle facilities, to traffic safety
and Intelligent Transportation Systems (ITS). Practical applications of the numerous regulatory and
guidance documents are brought to the class by the practicing engineers in a friendly and facilitated lectures
with plenty of interactive exercises. (“g”) (Del Campo)

SUBJECT: Instructional Materials Adoptions (Slavensky) - 7:50 p.m.

DEPARTMENT: Teaching and Learning

ACTION REQUESTED:
Discussion: The superintendent is recommending that the board discuss new instructional materials adoptions.
Action anticipated: April 22, 2025.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
It is essential that students and teachers continue to have access to current, standards-aligned instructional
materials that support rigorous, meaningful teaching and learning. To address this need, the Professional Learning
and Curriculum Innovation department recruited teachers and community members to review and recommend new
instructional materials. This presentation includes the following key information:
       The process committees used to review instructional materials and arrive at each recommendation.
       Information about the specific recommendations, including materials reviewed, criteria for review,
       community engagement efforts, and the total cost.
ATTACHMENT(S):

2. Report II: English 3 - Ethnic Studies
3. Report IIs: World Languages
4. Report IIs: History - Social Science
5. Reports IIs: Math

10.​   Considering the needs of district students, what are the strengths and
       limitations of the recommended materials?

       Strengths
       ●​ The materials are relevant and engaging.
       ●​ The materials are aligned with the four disciplines of ethnic studies identified
          in the model curriculum.
       ●​ The selection of materials provides experiences to students with varied
          genres of text.
       Limitations
       ●​ The materials do not come with a teacher guide.

11.​   What are the recommended materials?

​      The teacher evaluated the materials based on the Key Indicators and
       recommended Kindred, The Haunting of Hajji Hotak and Other Stories, They
       Called Us Enemy graphic novel, There There, and You Sound Like A White Girl.

       adoption.

   Program Organization
                                   ●​ Includes enough material to support the entirety of the course
                                   ●​ Presents information and instruction systematically and logically
                                      for standards, tasks, and assessments.
                                   ●​ Includes guidance for using all components of the program to
                                      support deep and meaningful student learning
                                   ●​ Includes helpful reference materials for teachers to use the
                                      program (clear table of contents, glossaries, unit/lesson

                                      retakes possible.

                                      instruction

                                      classroom
                                   ●​ Provides comprehensive support (scaffolding, modification) for
                                      teachers to provide effective instruction for special needs students
                                      and English learners.

                                      enhances learning
                                   ●​ Provides a variety of activities to facilitate retention and promote
                                      incorporation of objectives

   Teacher Support                 ●​ Provides logical, explicit instructional guidelines for teachers to
                                      follow

                                ●​ Provides homework suggestions that reinforce or extend

FEEDBACK RESULTS

10.​   Considering the needs of district students, what are the strengths and
       limitations of the recommended materials?

       Strengths
       ●​ 'Culture Note' is included in each section, offering essential cultural
          information that is rarely found in other Japanese textbooks.
       ●​ The easily accessible digital versions of textbooks and workbooks are highly
          useful.
       Limitations
       ●​ It takes time to learn the online platform for listening activities.
       ●​ Assessments could benefit from additional ways for students to demonstrate
          their proficiency.

FEEDBACK RESULTS

10.​   Considering the needs of district students, what are the strengths and
       limitations of the recommended materials?

       Strengths
          ●​ Dekiru! is the only Japanese textbook specifically designed for the AP
             Japanese exam.
          ●​ It provides practice in listening, speaking, reading, and writing in the same
             format as the actual test.
          ●​ The exercises are challenging enough for students who need to expand
             their vocabulary and improve their grammar.
       Limitations
          ●​ Additional practice opportunities would provide even more support to
             learners.

11.​   What were the results of the evaluation and what are the recommended
       materials? ​

​      The teacher evaluated the materials based on the Key Indicators and
       recommends Dekiru!

                                         Report II

SUMMARY INFORMATION FROM REPORT I

1.​   Subject area or course:

      Advanced Placement (AP) United States History

2.​   Recommended text(s):

      American History: Connecting with the Past, McGraw Hill, 2023

3.​   Rationale:

      a.​     Title, publisher, copyright and year of adoption of current textbook:

              The American Pageant, Cengage, 2015, adopted in 2017

      b.​     Alignment with state or district textbook cycle:

              The adoption of the AP United States History materials is off cycle with the
              current San Juan Unified adoption matrix.

      c.​     Special considerations, if any:

              The cycle was originally set for the 2023-2024 school year. The pilot was
              extended into late spring 2024 in order to collect additional data. Since the
              final committee meeting did not occur until April 2024, the materials were
              not able to be shared with the Board for action until the 2024-2025 school
              year.

4.​     Adoption timeline:

          Indicators document.

 9.​      In what ways were student responses solicited?

          At the end of each cycle, students who participated in the pilot responded to a
          survey. Strengths and limitations shared by students are as follows:

Strengths

     ●​ The students appreciated the assessment features.
     ●​ The students appreciated the reminders for upcoming assignment due dates.
     ●​ The students appreciated the Smartbook tool, specifically the self-rating of their
        confidence level for identified topics.

Limitations

     ●​ Some students disliked that teacher highlighted notes could not be shared.

          ●​ Community members were able to join the adoption committee.

               ○​ October 2, 2023 - January 8, 2024 - Information about the materials

                   review, plus availability for members of the community to view the
                   materials in person by appointment.
               ○​ September 21, 2023 - Table set up at the College Night at Rio

Textbook Adoption – Report II – Page 4
Advanced Placement (AP) United States History

FEEDBACK RESULTS

11.​   Considering the needs of district students, what are the strengths and
       limitations of the recommended materials?

       Strengths
       ●​ The materials are well-organized and aligned to the units of the College
          Board exam outline.
       ●​ The digital resources are accessible and helpful.
       ●​ The materials offer a wide breadth of material in various formats.
       Limitations
       ●​ Google integration was a challenge, though that is expected to be resolved
          with the full adoption.
       ●​ Teachers shared that more discussion-based questions would be desirable.

12.​   What were the results of the final voting and what are the recommended
       instructional materials?

​      Using a consensus model, 4 of 4 committee members support the
       recommendation of American History: Connecting with the Past, McGraw Hill,
       2023.

13.​   List all the student and teacher components of the program, both
       purchased and gratis.
​
       Student Components                         Teacher Components
       ●​ Student print edition                   ●​ Teacher print edition
       ●​ 7-year digital access for the student   ●​ 7-year digital access for the teacher
          platform                                   platform

14.​   What professional learning will be offered to teachers? What costs will be
       associated with the training?
​
       Teachers will have the opportunity to attend a 2-hour session with the publisher
       in May. Makeup training will be offered again in the fall for new teachers or those
       unable to attend.

​      The cost for the professional development as described above is included in the
       adoption.

Attachment B: Category Key Indicators for Advanced Placement United States History

 Category                Key Indicators
 Content/ Alignment to
 Standards                  ●​ Reflects and incorporates the content from the HSS Framework, Content
                               Standards - HSS, ELD Standards, CCSS Literacy Standards for HSS ,
                               Advanced Placement Standards (CollegeBoard)
                            ●​ Provides explicit, sequential, logical, systematic instruction and diagnostic
                               support
                            ●​ Reflects accurate content information

 Program Organization
                            ●​ Includes enough material to support the entirety of the course
                            ●​ Presents information and instruction systematically and logically for
                               standards, tasks, and assessments
                            ●​ Includes guidance for using all components of the program to support
                               deep and meaningful student learning
                            ●​ Includes helpful reference materials for teachers to use the program
                               (clear table of contents, glossaries, unit/lesson overviews, etc.)

 Assessment
                            ●​ Assesses understanding and application of skills and knowledge
                               embedded in the program
                            ●​ Assesses students in several formats (summative and formative) for
                               immediate follow-up instruction, practice, and review. Assessments
                               should have multiple forms making revisions and retakes possible
                            ●​ Helps teachers plan and determine the effectiveness of classroom
                               instruction
                            ●​ Assessments easily linked to google classroom
                            ●​ Assessment software accessible by both Mac and PC

 Universal Access
                            ●​ Provides resources and strategies that engage every student in the
                               classroom
                            ●​ Provides comprehensive support (scaffolding, modification) for teachers
                               to provide effective instruction for special needs students and English
                               learners
                                    o​ Online textbook/supports also available in Spanish and/or other
                                        languages
                                    o​ Instructors able to demonstrate online with a side-by-side view
                                        of texts in different languages, but working in the same chapter
                                        (for example, chapter 2 in English on the left and Arabic on the
                                        right)
                            ●​ Includes user friendly style/format (visual stimuli, graphics) that enhances
                               learning
                            ●​ Provides a variety of activities to facilitate retention and promote
                               incorporation of objectives




                                                                                                               174
Textbook Adoption – Report II – Page 8
Advanced Placement (AP) United States History

 Instructional Planning
 and Teacher Support        ●​ Provides logical, explicit instructional guidelines for teachers to follow
                            ●​ Includes a teacher planning guide explaining how to use components with
                               alternative schedules
                            ●​ Identifies specific objectives, instructional examples, and practice
                               opportunities in every lesson
                            ●​ Provides a list of necessary instructional materials for each lesson
                            ●​ Provides support/suggestions for the appropriate use of the program’s
                               technology

                            ●​ Includes electronic resources that are integral to the program, not
                               extraneous
                            ●​ Provides homework suggestions that reinforce or extend classroom
                               instruction

 Digital Tools/Online
 Resources                  ●​ Includes clear and sufficient guidance to support teaching and learning of
                               the targeted standards, including, when appropriate, the use of
                               technology and media
                            ●​ Technology components are easy to access and user friendly for students
                               and teachers
                                    o​ easily adaptable to a distance learning format, and/or
                                        independent study
                            ●​ Technology is available across multiple platforms and devices (i.e.
                               functionality for tablets, macs, PCs, Chromebooks, smartphones,
                               connection to Google Classroom, etc.)
                            ●​ Enhances student understanding in the appropriate grade level standards
                               and supports the print resources
                            ●​ Technology is interactive and adaptive when possible

 Social Content
                            ●​ Materials accurately and equitably portray diverse religions, diverse
 Social Justice Standards      cultures and races, various ages, people with varying abilities, as well as
                               diverse sexual orientations and diverse gender identities
 8 Point Commitment         ●​ Materials emphasize diverse groups of people in varied, positive, and
                               contributing roles
                            ●​ The print and/or online materials meet the diverse needs of all learners
                               (English learners, students with special needs, advanced learners, learning
                               styles, diverse cultures, additional languages as needed, etc.)

     RECOMMENDATION PROCESS

     7.​      List of adoption committee members:

     ​        See Attachment A: List of Committee Members

     8.​      What criteria did piloting teachers use to evaluate materials?

     ​        The adoption committee evaluated the materials using the Category Key
              Indicators document.

              See Attachment B: Category Key Indicators for High School AP World History

     9.​      In what ways were student responses solicited?

              At the end of each cycle, students who participated in the pilot responded to a
              survey. Strengths and limitations shared by students are as follows:

Strengths

   ●​ The students appreciated the user-friendly design of the materials.
   ●​ The students identified the variety of visuals, diagrams, and video resources available online.
   ●​ The students appreciated the study aids such as guided reading questions and quiz
      questions at the end of lessons.

Limitations

   ●​ Some students felt that the print materials were dense.
   ●​ Some students felt that the print materials didn’t include enough pictures.

FEEDBACK RESULTS

11.​   Considering the needs of district students, what are the strengths and
       limitations of the recommended materials?

       Strengths
       ●​ The materials are aligned to the College Board AP World History course
          exam.
       ●​ The materials are consumable and able to be annotated by students and
          updated annually to reflect any course exam revisions.
       Limitations
       ●​ The digital resources are not always intuitive.
       ●​ The materials are plain and without color due to being consumable.

12.​   What were the results of the final voting and what are the recommended
       instructional materials?

​      Using a consensus model, 3 of 3 committee members support the
       recommendation of AMSCO Advanced Placement Edition World History: Modern
       1200-Present.

13.​   List all the student and teacher components of the program, both
       purchased and gratis.
​
       Student Components                         Teacher Components
       ●​ 7-year Student Edition print (all       ●​ 7-year Teacher Resource Print
          consumables are paid for up front)      ●​ 7-year digital access for the
       ●​ 7-year digital access for the student      Teacher Interactive and eBook
          Interactive and eBook Bundle               Bundle

14.​   What professional learning will be offered to teachers? What costs will be
       associated with the training?
​
​      Teachers will have the opportunity to attend a 2-hour session with the publisher
       in May. Makeup training will be offered again in the fall for new teachers or those
       unable to attend.

       The cost for the professional development as described above is included in the
       adoption.

   and Teacher Support           ●​ Provides logical, explicit instructional guidelines for teachers
                                    to follow
                                 ●​ Includes a teacher planning guide explaining how to use
                                    components with alternative schedules
                                 ●​ Identifies specific objectives, instructional examples, and
                                    practice opportunities in every lesson
                                 ●​ Provides a list of necessary instructional materials for each
                                    lesson
                                 ●​ Provides support/suggestions for the appropriate use of the
                                    program’s technology

                                 ●​ Includes electronic resources that are integral to the
                                    program, not extraneous
                                 ●​ Provides homework suggestions that reinforce or extend
                                    classroom instruction

   Digital Tools/Online
   Resources                     ●​ Includes clear and sufficient guidance to support teaching
                                    and learning of the targeted standards, including, when
                                    appropriate, the use of technology and media
                                 ●​ Technology components are easy to access and user
                                    friendly for students and teachers
                                         o​ easily adaptable to a distance learning format,
                                             and/or independent study
                                 ●​ Technology is available across multiple platforms and
                                    devices (i.e. functionality for tablets, macs, PCs,
                                    Chromebooks, smartphones, connection to Google
                                    Classroom, etc.)
                                 ●​ Enhances student understanding in the appropriate grade
                                    level standards and supports the print resources
                                 ●​ Technology is interactive and adaptive when possible

   Social Content
                                 ●​ Materials accurately and equitably portray diverse religions,
   Social Justice Standards         diverse cultures and races, various ages, people with
                                    varying abilities, as well as diverse sexual orientations and
   8 Point Commitment               diverse gender identities
                                 ●​ Materials emphasize diverse groups of people in varied,
                                    positive, and contributing roles
                                 ●​ The print and/or online materials meet the diverse needs of
                                    all learners (English learners, students with special needs,
                                    advanced learners, learning styles, diverse cultures,
                                    additional languages as needed, etc.)

9. ​   What opportunities were provided for community input?

          ●​ Community members were able to join the adoption committee.
               ○​ February 6, 2024 - An application for committee participation was
                   shared via San Juan Scene newsletter.

                   Juan mobile app, and social media.

               ○​ October 1 - December 18, 2024 - Information about the materials
                   being considered for adoption, plus options for in-person and online
                   review, are made available on the San Juan website for community
                   review, plus availability for members of the community to view the

                   Americano High School.

FEEDBACK RESULTS

10.​   Considering the needs of district students, what are the strengths and
       limitations of the recommended materials?

       Strengths
       ●​ The materials are aligned with the College Board Advanced Placement (AP)
          Macroeconomics exam.
       ●​ The materials combine macroeconomics and microeconomics principles for
          thorough review.
       ●​ The materials are chunked and user-friendly.
       Limitations
       ●​ The inclusion of microeconomics makes for a larger textbook.

11.​   What are the recommended materials?

​      The teacher evaluated the materials based on the Category Key Indicators for
       Advanced Placement (AP) Macroeconomics and recommended Krugman’s
       Economics for the AP Course, 4th edition.

12.​  List all the student and teacher components of the program, both
      purchased and gratis.
Student Components                          Teacher Components
●​ Student print edition                    ●​ Teacher print edition
●​ 7-year digital access for the student    ●​ 7-year digital access for the teacher
   edition and platform                        edition and platform
                                            ●​ Test bank



                                                                                         194
Textbook Adoption – Report II – Page 4
Advanced Placement (AP) Macroeconomics



13.​   What professional learning will be offered to teachers? What costs will be
       associated with the training?
​
​      Teachers will have the opportunity to attend a 2-hour session with the publisher
       in May. Makeup training will be offered again in the fall for new teachers or those
       unable to attend.

​      The cost for the professional development as described above is included in the
       adoption.

FEEDBACK RESULTS

10.​   Considering the needs of district students, what are the strengths and
       limitations of the recommended materials?

       Strengths
       ●​ There are many formative assessment tools and teacher reports to guide
          instruction.
       ●​ The case reviews and free-response question rubrics are helpful.
       ●​ The document reader provides additional access to foundational documents.
       Limitations
       ●​ Quizlet is not yet available due to data privacy regulations.
       ●​ The online test generator makes it challenging to create paper assessments.

11.​   What were the results of the final voting and what are the recommended
       instructional materials?

​      After reviewing the materials, 3 of 3 committee members support the
       recommendation of American Government: Stories of a Nation with the
       Foundational Documents and Court Cases Reader, 2nd edition.

FEEDBACK RESULTS

10.​   Considering the needs of district students, what are the strengths and
       limitations of the recommended materials?

       Strengths
       ●​ The Field Guide and Your Turn field-work activities are useful in developing
          student skills to think like an anthropologist.
       ●​ The digital resources and tools are accessible and helpful.
       ●​ The tutorial How-Tos develop student skills and go deeper than content.
       ●​ The content is relevant, current, and engaging.
       Limitations
       ●​ There is more of a sociology focus than other materials reviewed.
       ●​ The materials seem like they are intended for the college level.

11.​   What were the results of the final voting and what are the recommended
       instructional materials?

​      After reviewing the materials, 2 of 2 committee members support the
       recommendation of Cultural Anthropology: A Toolkit for a Global Age, 4th edition
       with the Field Work Journal.

   Program Organization
                                 ●​ Includes enough material to support the entirety of the course
                                 ●​ Presents information and instruction systematically and logically
                                    for standards, tasks, and assessments
                                 ●​ Includes guidance for using all components of the program to
                                    support deep and meaningful student learning
                                 ●​ Includes helpful reference materials for teachers to use the
                                    program (clear table of contents, glossaries, unit/lesson
                                    overviews, etc.)

   Assessment
                                 ●​ Assesses understanding and application of skills and knowledge
                                    embedded in the program
                                 ●​ Assesses students in several formats (summative and formative)
                                    for immediate follow-up instruction, practice, and review.
                                    Assessments should have multiple forms making revisions and
                                    retakes possible
                                 ●​ Helps teachers plan and determine the effectiveness of classroom
                                    instruction
                                 ●​ Assessments easily linked to Google classroom
                                 ●​ Assessment software accessible by both Mac and PC

   Universal Access
                                 ●​ Provides resources and strategies that engage every student in the
                                    classroom
                                 ●​ Provides comprehensive support (scaffolding, modification) for
                                    teachers to provide effective instruction for special needs
                                    students and English learners
                                         o​ Online textbook/supports also available in other
                                             languages
                                         o​ Instructors able to demonstrate online with a
                                             side-by-side view of texts in different languages, but
                                             working in the same chapter (for example, chapter 2 in
                                             English on the left and Arabic on the right)

                                 ●​ Includes user-friendly style/format (visual stimuli, graphics) that

                                 ●​ Provides a variety of activities to facilitate retention and promote

   Instructional Planning and
   Teacher Support               ●​ Provides logical, explicit instructional guidelines for teachers to
                                    follow
                                 ●​ Includes a teacher planning guide explaining how to use
                                    components with alternative schedules
                                 ●​ Identifies specific objectives, instructional examples, and practice
                                    opportunities in every lesson
                                 ●​ Provides a list of necessary instructional materials for each lesson
                                 ●​ Provides support/suggestions for the appropriate use of the
                                    program’s technology

                                 ●​ Includes electronic resources that are integral to the program, not
                                    extraneous
                                 ●​ Provides homework suggestions that reinforce or extend
                                    classroom instruction

   Digital Tools/Online
   Resources                     ●​ Includes clear and sufficient guidance to support teaching and
                                    learning of the targeted standards, including, when appropriate,
                                    the use of technology and media
                                 ●​ Technology components are easy to access and user-friendly for
                                    students and teachers
                                         o​ easily adaptable to a distance learning format, and/or
                                             independent study
                                 ●​ Technology is available across multiple platforms and devices (i.e.

                                    connection to Google Classroom, etc.)
                                 ●​ Enhances student understanding in the appropriate grade level

                                 ●​ Technology is interactive and adaptive when possible

FEEDBACK RESULTS

10.​   Considering the needs of district students, what are the strengths and
       limitations of the recommended materials?

       Strengths
       ●​ The materials are accessible to a variety of learners.
       ●​ The content is relevant, current, and engaging.
       ●​ The assessment generator is user-friendly and provides a variety of
          assessment options.
       ●​ The materials are adaptable to multiple law courses.
       Limitations
       ●​ The materials are an overview of various aspects of law and legal principles.

11.​   What were the results of the final voting and what are the recommended
       instructional materials?

​      After reviewing the materials, 5 of 5 committee members support the
       recommendation of Street Law: A Course in Practical Law, 11th edition.

12.​   List all the student and teacher components of the program, both
       purchased and gratis.
​
       Student Components                             Teacher Components
       ●​ Student print edition                       ●​ Teacher print manual
       ●​ 6-year digital access for the student       ●​ 6-year digital access for the online
          platform                                       teacher edition

Textbook Adoption – Report II – Page 4
Constitutional Law, Political Science Criminal & Civil Law, and You & the Law



13.​   What professional learning will be offered to teachers? What costs will be
       associated with the training?
​
​      Teachers will have the opportunity to attend a 2-hour session with the publisher
       in May. Makeup training will be offered again in the fall for new teachers or those
       unable to attend.

​      The cost for the professional development as described above is included in the
       adoption.

Limitations

FEEDBACK RESULTS

11.​   Considering the needs of district students, what are the strengths and
       limitations of the recommended materials?

       Strengths
       ●​ The content relates higher-level math and financial topics well.
       ●​ The digital resources are easy to modify to meet students' diverse needs.
       ●​ The activities are up-to-date, relevant, and responsive to different learning
          styles.
       Limitations
       ●​ Some lessons do not provide a sufficient question bank for additional
          practice.
       ●​ Some lessons lack the necessary vocabulary scaffolds.

12.​   What were the results of the final voting and what are the recommended
       instructional materials?

​      Using a consensus model, 4 of 4 committee members support the
       recommendation of Financial Algebra.

13.​   List all the student and teacher components of the program, both
       purchased and gratis.
​
       Student Components                         Teacher Components
       ●​ Student edition                         ●​ Teacher’s edition
       ●​ Online digital access to Next Gen       ●​ Online digital access to Next Gen
          Personal Finance (www.ngpf.org)            Personal Finance (www.ngpf.org)

14.​   What professional learning will be offered to teachers? What costs will be
       associated with the training?
​
​      Teachers will have the opportunity to attend a 3-hour session with the publisher
       and a 3-hour session to collaborate with colleagues in June or August. Additional




                                                                                           226
Textbook Adoption – Report II – Page 5
Financial Math



       training modules are offered through Next Gen Personal Finance. All
       professional learning will be provided by Next Gen Personal Finance at no cost.

       ●​ The resources are easily modified to differentiate for all learners.
       ●​ The lessons are easy to follow and promote student collaboration.
       Limitations
       ●​ Some lessons rely heavily on reading and vocabulary without sufficient
          scaffolds.

12.​   What were the results of the final voting and what are the recommended
       instructional materials?

​      Using a consensus model, 4 of 4 committee members support the
       recommendation of Math Medic.

13.​   List all the student and teacher components of the program, both
       purchased and gratis.
​
       Student Components                         Teacher Components
       ●​ Student edition                         ●​ Teacher’s edition


14.​   What professional learning will be offered to teachers? What costs will be
       associated with the training?
​
​      Teachers will have the opportunity to attend a 3-hour session with the publisher
       and a 3-hour session to collaborate with colleagues in June or August. Makeup
       training will be offered again in the fall for new teachers or those unable to attend
       the summer sessions.

​      The cost for the professional development is $8,000.

15.​   Curriculum department contact for additional information:

​      Nicole Kukral, Director, Professional Learning and Curriculum Innovation
​      nkukral@sanjuan.edu
​      (916) 979-8934

16.​   Date submitted Report II: March 19, 2025

    Attachment B: Category Key Indicators for Mathematical Modeling

Category        Key Indicators
Content/         ●​ Reflects and incorporates the content from the identified California Common
Alignment to        Core State Standards from Integrated Math 1 and Integrated Math 2
Standards        ●​ Provides explicit, sequential, logical, systematic instruction and diagnostic
                    support, scaffolded content provides accessibility for students of all levels
                 ●​ Reflects accurate content information
                 ●​ Provide opportunities for students to engage using their personal
                    experiences
Program          ●​ Includes enough material to support the entirety of the course
Organization     ●​ Presents information and instruction systematically and logically for
                    standards, tasks, and assessments
                 ●​ Includes guidance for using all components of the program to support deep
                    and meaningful student learning
                 ●​ Includes helpful reference materials for teachers to use the program (clear
                    table of contents, glossaries, unit/lesson overviews, etc.)
Assessment       ●​ Assesses understanding and application of skills and knowledge embedded
                    in the program, including foundational skills
                 ●​ Assesses students in several formats (summative and formative) for
                    immediate follow-up instruction, practice, and review. Assessments should
                    have multiple forms making revisions and retakes possible.
                 ●​ Performance Tasks have instructional guidance, scaffolding, and
                    identification of skills/standards
                 ●​ Helps teachers plan and determine the effectiveness of classroom
                    instruction
Universal        ●​ Provides resources and strategies that engage every student in the
Access              classroom
                 ●​ Provides comprehensive support (scaffolding, modification) for teachers to
                    provide effective instruction for special needs students and English learners
                 ●​ Includes user-friendly style/format (visual stimuli, graphics) that enhances
                    learning. Addresses a variety of learning styles/modalities
                 ●​ Provides a variety of activities to facilitate retention and promote
                    incorporation of objectives
Instructional    ●​ Provides logical, explicit instructional guidelines for teachers to follow
Planning         ●​ Includes a teacher planning guide explaining how to use components with
and Teacher         alternative schedules
Support          ●​ Identifies specific objectives, instructional examples, and practice
                    opportunities in every lesson
                 ●​ Provides a list of necessary instructional materials for each lesson
                 ●​ Provides support/suggestions for the appropriate use of the program’s
                    technology
                 ●​ Includes electronic resources that are integral to the program, not
                    extraneous

                ●​ Technology components are easy to access and user-friendly for students

SAN JUAN UNIFIED SCHOOL DISTRICT                                       AGENDA ITEM:                      J.4
BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                       MEETING DATE:                 04/08/2025

SUBJECT: Public Hearing No. 1: New Pacific Charter - Arden Arcade Charter School Application (Oaxaca) -
8:05 p.m.

DEPARTMENT: Teaching and Learning

ACTION REQUESTED:
Public Hearing/Discussion: The superintendent is recommending that the board hold a public hearing and discuss
the New Pacific Charter - Arden Arcade charter school petition. New Pacific Charter - Arden Arcade is seeking a
five-year term commencing on July 1, 2025 through June 30, 2030. Action anticipated: May 27, 2025.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
New Pacific Charter has operated across the Sacramento region since 2005. The focus of the charter is early
literacy, and they also have dual and concurrent enrollment in their high school grades.

The district’s charter review team is thoroughly reviewing the charter petition, and New Pacific Charter has
provided all necessary information requested during the review process. The New Pacific Charter petition
presented to the Board of Education is in compliance with district Board Policy 0420.4, Charter Schools, and
current law. In order to recommend the approval of a charter school petition to the Board of Education, San Juan
Unified staff must determine that the charter school has met the requirements set forth in Education Code, Section
47605. For clarity, these requirements have been organized into the following four criteria, outlined in this section.

  I. Has the charter school presented a sound educational program?
 II. Is the charter school demonstrably likely to successfully implement the proposed educational program?
III. Is the petition reasonably comprehensive?
IV. Is the charter school serving all students who wish to attend?

A copy of the charter petition is available for review in the superintendent's office and at the San Juan Central
enrollment office.

ATTACHMENT(S):
1. Presentation

BOARD COMMITTEE ACTION/COMMENT:
N/A

Superintendent's Cabinet: 03/31/2025

No Direct Costs

BOARD OF EDUCATION

                                                                   MEETING DATE:                04/08/2025

SUBJECT: Proposed Board Meeting Dates 2025-2026 (Board) - 8:20 p.m.

DEPARTMENT: Administration

ACTION REQUESTED:
Action: The superintendent is recommending that the board review and approve the proposed board meeting dates
for the 2025-2026 school year.

RATIONALE/BACKGROUND:
Regular board meetings are held on the second and fourth Tuesday of each month, unless noted otherwise. There
are no regular board meetings held in July. Due to the holiday and winter break, the superintendent is proposing
that one (regular) meeting be held during the months of November and December. In election years, the December
meeting must take place after the second Friday in December in order to comply with Education Code 35143.

      August 12, 2025
      August 26, 2025
      September 9, 2025
      September 23, 2025
      October 14, 2025
      October 28, 2025
      November 18, 2025 (3rd Tuesday)
      December 16, 2025 (3rd Tuesday)
